## Management Summary

### Verdict

🔴 Not production-ready. The application stores authentication credentials with weak, reversible hashing, commits cryptographic signing keys in source code, and trusts attacker-controlled input in multiple query-construction paths - any of which an unauthenticated user can exploit independently. The architecture concentrates session state, data access, and privileged-route logic in a single backend monolith with no server-side authorization layer, so a single exploited boundary delivers full database and session access.

**Risk distribution:** 🔴 Critical: 9 · 🟠 High: 44 · 🟡 Medium: 17 · 🟢 Low: 0 · **Total: 70**


<br/>

**Concrete scenarios an attacker can execute today, each without access to source code:**

<blockquote style="border-left: 3px solid #dc2626; background: #fef2f2; padding: 16px 20px; margin: 0;">

- **Admin account takeover without credentials** — The hardcoded signing key committed to the repository lets any attacker mint a valid admin session token offline and immediately authenticate as administrator — no brute force or phishing required. *(🔴 [F-007](#f-007), 🔴 [F-008](#f-008))*
- **Full customer database dump via login form** — User-supplied email in the login request is concatenated directly into a database query, allowing an unauthenticated attacker to extract all customer records, password hashes, and payment data in a single request. *(🔴 [F-001](#f-001), 🟠 [F-053](#f-053))*
- **Arbitrary file read from the server via uploaded XML** — The order-receipt upload parser processes external entity declarations, so an attacker can retrieve any file the server process can read — including environment files and private keys — by uploading a crafted XML document. *(🔴 [F-012](#f-012))*
- **Remote code execution via product-review sandbox** — The server evaluates customer-supplied review content as JavaScript using a sandboxed eval that can be escaped, giving any authenticated user the ability to run arbitrary code in the server process. *(🔴 [F-013](#f-013), 🟠 [F-024](#f-024))*
- **Any user can read or modify another customer's account** — Object references in API requests are trusted without checking ownership, so a logged-in attacker can enumerate and modify any account, order, or review by incrementing the identifier in the request. *(🔴 [F-010](#f-010), 🔴 [F-002](#f-002))*
- **Password database cracked offline after SQL injection** — Passwords are hashed with an unsalted, single-pass algorithm that is indexable against public rainbow tables, so the credential dump obtained via injection yields plaintext passwords for the majority of accounts within hours. *(🔴 [F-011](#f-011))*
- **Persistent cross-site attack persists for every visitor** — Output sanitization is deliberately disabled in the Angular template layer, so a stored payload — submitted once through product reviews or user profiles — executes in every subsequent visitor's browser session. *(🔴 [F-025](#f-025), 🔴 [F-035](#f-035))*

</blockquote>

<br/>

Remediation must address the structural root causes first - rotating the committed signing key, parameterizing all query construction, enforcing server-side ownership checks on every data-access route, and enabling output encoding - before the application handles real customer data.

**Attack-chain analysis.** 6 findings anchor 4 code-verified attack chains (see [§8](#8-abuse-cases) Abuse Cases): 🔴 [F-002](#f-002) — Systemic Mass Assignment of Privileged Fields (`verify.ts:51`), 🔴 [F-005](#f-005) — Sensitive Routes Registered Without Authorization (`server.ts:310`), 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — Insecure JWT Verification (`insecurity.ts:55`), 🔴 [F-010](#f-010) — Insecure Direct Object Reference (`dataExport.ts:26`), 🔴 [F-035](#f-035) — Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) (`search-result.component.ts:143`), 🔴 [F-046](#f-046) — Insecure Client-Side Storage of JWT in localStorage (`oauth.component.ts:51`). 3 of these are rated above their individual baseline as a direct result of the verified chain.

### Architectural Anti-Patterns

The defects below are structural - each spans multiple findings and requires a design change, not a point fix. See **[§6 Security Architecture](#6-security-architecture)** for the per-control detail.

- **SPA without BFF** — The Angular SPA stores the session JWT in browser localStorage where any same-origin script can read it; there is no Backend-for-Frontend to hold the credential server-side in an HttpOnly cookie, so a single XSS payload converts to full session takeover for every active user.
    - _Affected components:_ [C-01](#c-01), [C-02](#c-02)
    - _Findings:_ 🔴 [F-046](#f-046) — JWT stored in localStorage (`oauth.component.ts:51`), 🟠 [F-047](#f-047) — Session Token in Non-HttpOnly Cookie (`oauth.component.ts:50`), 🔴 [F-025](#f-025) — Persistent XSS surface (`server.ts:188`)

- **Secrets hardcoded in source** — The RSA private signing key, HMAC secrets for coupon and deluxe-membership tokens, and the 2FA signing key are all committed to the repository, meaning any contributor or repo clone yields material sufficient to forge arbitrary authentication tokens and business-logic tokens.
    - _Affected components:_ [C-03](#c-03), [C-02](#c-02)
    - _Findings:_ 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — Hardcoded Cryptographic Key (`insecurity.ts:21`), 🔴 [F-017](#f-017) — Hardcoded HMAC keys for coupon and deluxe tokens (`insecurity.ts:42`), 🔴 [F-015](#f-015) — Weak 2FA Token Signing Key (`2fa.ts:20`)

- **Raw SQL string interpolation** — Multiple routes bypass the Sequelize ORM and interpolate request parameters directly into SQL strings; the pattern recurs across the login, search, and review endpoints so it is a structural authoring practice, not an isolated omission.
    - _Affected components:_ [C-02](#c-02), [C-04](#c-04)
    - _Findings:_ 🔴 [F-001](#f-001) — Systemic SQL Injection (`login.ts:34`), 🟠 [F-053](#f-053) — In-process SQLite gives injection full blast radius (`index.ts:41`)

- **Missing server-side authorization layer** — Route authorization is implemented client-side through Angular guards and server-side only through a JWT presence check, without an ownership or role assertion on the actual resource; every object-access endpoint trusts the id supplied by the caller.
    - _Affected components:_ [C-02](#c-02), [C-01](#c-01)
    - _Findings:_ 🔴 [F-005](#f-005) — Sensitive Routes Without Authorization (`server.ts:310`), 🟠 [F-006](#f-006) — Client-Side-Only Access Control (`app.guard.ts:52`), 🔴 [F-010](#f-010) — Insecure Direct Object Reference (`dataExport.ts:26`), 🔴 [F-050](#f-050) — Authorization on Unverified Decoded Claims (`insecurity.ts:156`)

### AI / LLM Exposure

The application embeds an OpenAI-compatible LLM chatbot whose prompt construction, tool invocation, and output handling are all reachable by unauthenticated user input.

This system embeds an LLM / AI-agent surface. The risks below are architectural - each follows from how untrusted input reaches an AI sink (prompt, tool call, retrieval, model supply chain). See **[§6 Security Architecture](#6-security-architecture)** for the per-control detail.

- **LLM01 Prompt Injection** — User chat messages are concatenated directly into the prompt sent to the LLM without sanitization or structural separation, allowing an attacker to override chatbot instructions and obtain unauthorized discount coupons or other privileged actions. _([C-07](#c-07))_
  - ↳ 🟠 [F-029](#f-029) — Prompt Injection (`chat.ts:191`)
  - ↳ 🟠 [F-026](#f-026) — Indirect prompt injection in chatbot grants unauthorized coupons (`chat.ts:205`)

- **LLM06 Excessive Agency** — The chatbot can invoke backend tool-calls (coupon issuance, order placement) without a human-in-the-loop confirmation gate, so a successful prompt injection immediately produces real side-effects rather than only information disclosure. _([C-07](#c-07))_
  - ↳ 🔴 [F-051](#f-051) — Excessive Agency in LLM Tool Invocation (`chat.ts:176`)
  - ↳ 🟠 [F-028](#f-028) — Insecure Handling of LLM Tool-Call Output (`chat.ts:181`)

- **LLM07 System Prompt Leakage** — The chatbot's system prompt embeds confidential discount rules and internal business logic; an attacker who asks the model to repeat its instructions can extract these commercial rules without any authentication. _([C-07](#c-07))_
  - ↳ 🟠 [F-039](#f-039) — System Prompt Leakage of Confidential Discount Rule (`chat.ts:105`)

- **LLM02 Sensitive Information Disclosure** — Conversation history is accepted from the client without integrity verification, so an attacker can inject fabricated prior turns into the session, potentially extracting information or steering model behavior based on invented context. _([C-07](#c-07))_
  - ↳ 🟠 [F-018](#f-018) — Unvalidated Conversation History Trust (`chat.ts:191`)

**Threat actors.** The actors below drive the numbered attack paths in the figures above. The **Shop User** is the *victim* of client-side attacks (XSS / CSRF), not an attacker - in Figure 2 the compromise surfaces as the resulting business-impact node rather than as a separate actor box.

- **Shop User** — legitimate customer; target of client-side attacks; target of ⑥ Output Encoding / Cross-Site Scripting, ⑦ CSRF / Permissive CORS.
- **Anonymous Internet Attacker** — no account; registers in seconds when needed; drives ① Insecure Query Construction & Data Access, ② Hardcoded Secrets & Weak Cryptography, ④ Sensitive File & Secret Exposure.
- **Authenticated Internet Attacker** — owns a regular account; logged in; drives ③ Broken Authorization & Access Control, ⑤ Remote Code Execution (unsafe eval).

**7 structural threats**, grouped by weakness class - each row is one threat, not one finding. *Threat Description* states the general architectural weakness (STRIDE in brackets); *Findings* lists the concrete instances, each linked to [§7 Findings Register](#7-findings-register) with its component; *Risk & Impact* combines severity with business consequence.

| <a id="path-sensitive-data-exposure"></a>④ | **Sensitive File & Secret Exposure** _(I)_<br/>Unsalted password hashing, cleartext payment storage, public FTP directory listing, and session tokens stored in browser-accessible locations expose customer credentials and payment data to unauthenticated retrieval. | <span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-003](#f-003)</span> - Sensitive Error Detail Disclosure Across Endpoints (`server.ts:682`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-02](#c-02)</span>&nbsp;Express REST API Monolith<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🔴&nbsp;[F-011](#f-011)</span> - Unsalted MD5 password storage (`user.ts:76`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-04](#c-04)</span>&nbsp;Data Persistence Layer<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-022](#f-022)</span> - Open Redirect via substring allowlist (`insecurity.ts:136`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-03](#c-03)</span>&nbsp;Authentication & Identity Subsystem<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-033](#f-033)</span> - Zip Slip Path Traversal on Archive Extraction (`fileUpload.ts:34`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-05](#c-05)</span>&nbsp;File Upload & Parser Subsystem<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-036](#f-036)</span> - Arbitrary Field Selection Leaks Sensitive User Data (`currentUser.ts:30`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-03](#c-03)</span>&nbsp;Authentication & Identity Subsystem<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-037](#f-037)</span> - Public directory listing and file download under /ftp (`server.ts:269`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-02](#c-02)</span>&nbsp;Express REST API Monolith<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-039](#f-039)</span> - System Prompt Leakage of Confidential Discount Rule (`chat.ts:105`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-07](#c-07)</span>&nbsp;AI Chatbot Service<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-044](#f-044)</span> - Payment card number stored in cleartext (`card.ts:38`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-04](#c-04)</span>&nbsp;Data Persistence Layer<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-045](#f-045)</span> - Challenge Flag Leak on WebSocket Connect (`registerWebsocketEvents.ts:30`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-08](#c-08)</span>&nbsp;Socket\.IO Real-Time Channel<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟡&nbsp;[F-062](#f-062)</span> - | <a id="path-remote-code-execution"></a>⑤ | **Remote Code Execution (unsafe eval)** _(E)_<br/>Server-side evaluation of attacker-supplied content and a prototype-pollution path through the sandbox boundary enable authenticated users to execute arbitrary code in the server process. | <span style="white-space:nowrap">🔴&nbsp;[F-013](#f-013)</span> - Server-Side Code Evaluation of Untrusted Input (`b2bOrder.ts:23`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-06](#c-06)</span>&nbsp;B2B v2 Order API<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-024](#f-024)</span> - Prototype Pollution via Sandbox Escape (`b2bOrder.ts:23`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-06](#c-06)</span>&nbsp;B2B v2 Order API<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-026](#f-026)</span> - Indirect prompt injection in chatbot grants unauthorized coupons (`chat.ts:205`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-02](#c-02)</span>&nbsp;Express REST API Monolith<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-028](#f-028)</span> - Insecure Handling of LLM Tool-Call Output (`chat.ts:181`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-07](#c-07)</span>&nbsp;AI Chatbot Service<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-033](#f-033)</span> - Zip Slip Path Traversal on Archive Extraction (`fileUpload.ts:34`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-05](#c-05)</span>&nbsp;File Upload & Parser Subsystem<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-034](#f-034)</span> - Stored Payload via Weak Upload Validation (`profileImageUrlUpload.ts:29`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-05](#c-05)</span>&nbsp;File Upload & Parser Subsystem | 🔴 **Critical**<br/>Full Server Compromise | <span style="white-space:nowrap"><span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-013](#m-013)</span><br/><span style="white-space:nowrap"><span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-024](#m-024)</span> |
| <a id="path-cross-site-scripting"></a>⑥ | **Output Encoding / Cross-Site Scripting** _(T·I)_<br/>Output sanitization is disabled in the Angular template layer and upload validation is insufficient, allowing stored payloads to execute in every subsequent visitor's browser context. | <span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-025](#f-025)</span> - Persistent XSS surface left open by disabled XSS protections (`server.ts:188`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-02](#c-02)</span>&nbsp;Express REST API Monolith<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-035](#f-035)</span> - Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) (`search-result.component.ts:143`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-01](#c-01)</span>&nbsp;Angular Single-Page Application<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-038](#f-038)</span> - Wildcard CORS reflects any origin with credentials path (`server.ts:183`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-02](#c-02)</span>&nbsp;Express REST API Monolith<br/><span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-046](#f-046)</span> - Insecure Client-Side Storage of JWT in localStorage (`oauth.component.ts:51`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-01](#c-01)</span>&nbsp;Angular Single-Page Application | 🟠 **High**<br/>Customer Session Hijack | <span style="white-space:nowrap"><span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-025](#m-025)</span><br/><span style="white-space:nowrap"><span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-035](#m-035)</span> |
| <a id="path-cross-site-request-forgery"></a>⑦ | **CSRF / Permissive CORS** _(S·T)_<br/>a permissive CORS policy plus missing anti-CSRF tokens let any external page issue authenticated state-changing requests in the victim's session. | <span style="white-space:nowrap">🟠&nbsp;[F-038](#f-038)</span> - Wildcard CORS reflects any origin with credentials path (`server.ts:183`) <span style="white-space:nowrap">→&nbsp;[C-02](#c-02)</span>&nbsp;Express REST API Monolith | 🟠 **High**<br/>Customer Session Hijack | <span style="white-space:nowrap"><span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-038](#m-038)</span> |

_STRIDE: S spoofing · T tampering · R repudiation · I information disclosure · D denial of service · E elevation of privilege. Risk, findings, components, impact and Fix are derived deterministically; only the one-line weakness description is authored._

**Verified attack chains.** 4 fully viable ([AC-T-001](#ac-t-001), [AC-T-002](#ac-t-002), [AC-T-003](#ac-t-003), [AC-T-004](#ac-t-004)); 2 partially blocked ([AC-T-005](#ac-t-005), [AC-T-006](#ac-t-006)). These chains combine individual findings into end-to-end exploitation paths verified step-by-step against the code - see [§8 Abuse Cases](#8-abuse-cases) for the per-step breakdown and blocking mitigations.

**Bottom line:** These controls narrow specific attack surfaces but none eliminates a Critical finding on its own.

---

## 1. System Overview

Probably the most modern and sophisticated insecure web application

**Repository:** https://github.com/juice-shop/juice-`shop.git`
**Runtime:** `Node\.js` 22 - 26

### Scope

This threat model covers 10 components of juice-shop: **Angular Single-Page Application**, **Express REST API Monolith**, **Authentication & Identity Subsystem**, **Data Persistence Layer**, **File Upload & Parser Subsystem**, **B2B v2 Order API**, **AI Chatbot Service**, **Socket\.IO Real-Time Channel**, **CI/CD & Source-Contribution Integrity**, **Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface**.

All 10 modeled components received full STRIDE threat analysis.

**Out of scope:** third-party hosted dependencies, browser runtime, operating-system kernel, and the underlying network infrastructure.

---

<a id="identified-actors"></a>
### Identified Actors

| ID | Label | Layer | Status | Findings | Relevant for |
|--------|----------------------|--------------------|--------|----------------|----------------------|
| `ACT-D-01` | anonymous-internet-attacker | plugin | active | 4 | auth-identity, web3-nft |
| `ACT-D-02` | authenticated-low-priv-user | plugin | active | 3 | auth-identity, web3-nft |
| `ACT-D-03` | authenticated-high-priv-user | plugin | active | 0 | _(no findings)_ |
| `ACT-D-06` | supply-chain-attacker | plugin | active | 6 | ci-cd-pipeline |
| `ACT-D-07` | compromised-third-party-service | plugin | active | 1 | auth-identity |
| `ACT-D-08` | physical-device-holder | plugin | active | 8 | frontend-spa |
| `ACT-X-1` | prompt-injector | discovery (proposed) | proposed | 0 | _(no findings)_ |
| `ACT-X-2` | llm-provider-adversary | discovery (proposed) | proposed | 5 | chat-llm |
| `ACT-X-3` | ctf-competitor-security-researcher | discovery (proposed) | proposed | 0 | _(no findings)_ |
| `ACT-X-4` | ai-assistant-config-author | discovery (proposed) | proposed | 4 | ci-cd-pipeline |

#### Newly identified actors — please confirm

The following actors were proposed by LLM discovery (Phase 2.7) and are active in this run. Promote them to `.appsec/actors.yaml` to stabilize them across re-runs (`actors.md` [§7](#7-findings-register)).

- **`ACT-X-1` (prompt-injector)** — Section 7.13 confirms LLM surface: @ai-sdk/openai-compatible v2.0.35 powers /api/chat. Challenge metadata at `data/static/challenges.yml:1522` explicitly encodes a prompt injection challenge ('system prompts are just guidelines'). User input flows directly into LLM prompt with no sanitization observed. This actor is structurally distinct from ACT-D-01 (anonymous attacker) because prompt injection requires understanding of LLM prompt construction and targets the AI reasoning layer, not the web application layer.
- **`ACT-X-2` (llm-provider-adversary)** — Section 7.13 and component-hints: chat-llm-service deployed in cloud-saas zone; calls external OpenAI-compatible API. A compromised or rogue LLM provider can return adversarially crafted completions that trigger XSS in rendered output, exfiltrate conversation context, or manipulate application logic if completions are interpreted as instructions. ACT-D-07 covers compromised third-party services generically but does not model the unique AI completion trust boundary where completions are rendered or actioned differently from structured API responses.
- **`ACT-X-3` (ctf-competitor-security-researcher)** — Section 1 (Application Purpose): Juice Shop is explicitly designed for CTF competitions, security training, and tool evaluation. CTF competitors intentionally exploit every vulnerability in the app. This actor differs from ACT-D-01/ACT-D-02 in that they (a) have explicit authorization to exploit, (b) target all intentional vulnerability classes simultaneously, and (c) may attempt to enumerate/solve all ~100 challenges including privilege escalation to admin. This actor class is structurally relevant for scoping which findings are 'by design' vs. unintentional escapes. Threat models that conflate this actor with a malicious attacker will incorrectly prioritize intentional vulnerabilities.
- **`ACT-X-4` (ai-assistant-config-author)** — Section 7.28: The repo contains committed AI assistant configurations (.claude/CLAUDE.md, .cursor/rules, .continue/instructions.md, .ai/skills/ with verify-challenge/add-solution/add-reference skill files). An attacker with write access to these files can inject malicious directives that cause AI coding assistants to introduce vulnerabilities, exfiltrate code context, or override safety behaviors for all developers using those tools. This is an insider-adjacent supply chain vector not covered by ACT-D-06 (which targets npm/build artifacts) or ACT-D-07 (external service compromise).

#### Actors flagged for review

Discovery flagged these actors as questionable - recon shows no plausible reach for them in this repo. Consider disabling in your next run.

- **`ACT-D-08`** — ACT-D-08 is framed around physical/local-fs access to extract credentials from client-device or mobile-device storage. The recon evidence (Section 6.6, 7.10) shows JWT in browser localStorage — but the realistic threat path is remote XSS-based token theft, not physical device seizure and offline localStorage extraction. Juice Shop is a web application with no mobile wrapper (Section 7.29: mobile surface NOT DETECTED). The physical device holder attack path (attacker seizes device, reads IndexedDB/localStorage files from disk) is low-probability for this use case; the same token theft impact is already covered more accurately under ACT-D-01 exploiting DOM-based XSS sinks. The activation signal has_client_storage correctly fires but the actor framing (physical device, local-fs, mobile-device) does not match the actual deployment model. _(recommendation: review_for_disable)_

---

## 2. Architecture Diagrams

### 2.1 System Context

Who interacts with juice-shop from the outside, and through which channels. Solid arrows show normal usage; dashed red arrows mark unauthenticated probing or exploit paths (C4 Level 1).

**Key takeaway:** Every actor in the context interacts with juice-shop through its external interface, so authentication and input validation at that edge govern the entire attack surface.

## 3. Attack Walkthroughs

This section walks through how the highest-risk findings are exploited - one short walkthrough per Critical, each with attack steps, a focused sequence diagram, and the primary mitigation. The cross-finding view (which weaknesses combine toward the worst-case goal, and where one fix severs several paths) is in the [Critical Attack Tree](#critical-attack-tree). Full per-finding context - severity rationale, assets, detection signals - is in the [§7 Findings Register](#7-findings-register) row for each finding.

### 3.1 Systemic SQL Injection via String Interpolation

**Source:** 🔴 [F-001](#f-001) — `routes/login.ts:34`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html)). STRIDE: Tampering. See [§7 F-001](#f-001) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. `routes/login.ts:34` builds the authentication query by string interpolation: `SELECT * FROM Users WHERE email = '${req.body.email`}' AND password = '${`security.hash(req.body.password)`}' AND deletedAt IS NULL, executed via `models.sequelize.query` with plain:true.
2. Submitting email of ' OR 1=1-- closes the email literal and comments out the password and deletedAt clauses, returning the first user row (the seeded admin).
3. The handler at `login.ts:47` then issues a full admin token through afterLogin without ever checking the password.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant API
    participant DB
    Note over API: auth-identity - routes/login.ts:34
    Note over DB: Database
    Attacker->>API: Crafted HTTP request to the affected endpoint with classical OR 1=1 payload
    API->>DB: SQL built by string interpolation - payload becomes query
    DB-->>API: First matching row regardless of intended predicate
    API-->>Attacker: 200 OK with authenticated session / leaked rows
    alt Current state — F-001
        Attacker->>API: Crafted request exploiting F-001 succeeds
        API-->>Attacker: Exploitation confirmed
    else After M-001 — Establish dependency-update SLA and automated scanning polic
        Attacker->>API: Same request after the fix is applied
        API-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-001](#m-001) (Establish dependency-update SLA and automated scanning polic) lands, 🔴 [F-001](#f-001) is exploitable at `routes/login.ts:34` (Critical-severity, [CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-001](#m-001) (Establish dependency-update SLA and automated scanning policy)

### 3.2 Systemic Mass Assignment of Privileged Fields

**Source:** 🔴 [F-002](#f-002) — `routes/verify.ts:51`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-915](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/915.html)). STRIDE: Elevation of Privilege. See [§7 F-002](#f-002) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. Registration at POST /api/Users is handled by the auto-generated finale REST resource (`server.ts:408-422`) which passes the request body straight to UserModel.create.
2. The model's role attribute (`models/user.ts:79`) defaults to 'customer' but its validator isIn permits 'admin'.
3. Nothing strips role from the request body, so POST /api/Users with {email,password,passwordRepeat,role:'admin'} creates an administrator account. registerAdminChallenge (`routes/verify.ts:51`) only flags that this happened - it does not block it.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: auth-identity - routes/verify.ts:51
    Attacker->>App: Crafted request exercising the weakness at routes/verify.ts line 51
    App->>App: Vulnerable branch executes without the missing control
    App-->>Attacker: Response confirms the weakness - CWE-915
    alt Current state — F-002
        Attacker->>App: Crafted request exploiting F-002 succeeds
        App-->>Attacker: Exploitation confirmed
    else After M-002 — Implement centralized input validation and output encoding m
        Attacker->>App: Same request after the fix is applied
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-002](#m-002) (Implement centralized input validation and output encoding m) lands, 🔴 [F-002](#f-002) is exploitable at `routes/verify.ts:51` (Critical-severity, [CWE-915](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/915.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-002](#m-002) (Implement centralized input validation and output encoding middleware)

### 3.3 Hardcoded Cryptographic Key

**Source:** 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — `lib/insecurity.ts:21`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-321](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/321.html)). STRIDE: Spoofing. See [§7 F-007](#f-007) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. The RSA private key used to sign every JWT is a string literal at `lib/insecurity.ts:21`, committed to the public OWASP Juice Shop repository. `authorize()` at `insecurity.ts:54` signs tokens with this key via `jwt.sign(user, privateKey, {algorithm: 'RS256'})`.
2. Anyone who clones the repo can mint a valid token offline: `jwt.sign`({data:{id:1,email:'admin@juice-`sh.op`',role:'admin'}}, privateKey, {algorithm:'RS256'}).
3. The server accepts it at `verify()` (`insecurity.ts:55`) because the public key in encryptionkeys/jwt.pub is the matching half.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant Repo
    participant App
    Note over Repo: Public repository
    Note over App: auth-identity - lib/insecurity.ts:21
    Attacker->>Repo: Clone or browse - extract private key from lib/insecurity.ts line 21
    Attacker->>Attacker: Sign forged token / signature with the extracted key
    Attacker->>App: Submit forged artefact in normal authentication flow
    App-->>Attacker: Request accepted as authentic - signature validates
    alt Current state — F-007
        Attacker->>Repo: Crafted request exploiting F-007 succeeds
        Repo-->>Attacker: Exploitation confirmed
    else After M-007 — Load the JWT signing key from a secret manager and rotate th
        Attacker->>Repo: Same request after the fix is applied
        Repo-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-007](#m-007) (Load the JWT signing key from a secret manager and rotate th) lands, 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) is exploitable at `lib/insecurity.ts:21` (Critical-severity, [CWE-321](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/321.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-007](#m-007) (Load the JWT signing key from a secret manager and rotate the leaked key)

### 3.4 Insecure JWT Verification

**Source:** 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — `lib/insecurity.ts:55`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-347](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/347.html)). STRIDE: Spoofing. See [§7 F-008](#f-008) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. `verify()` at `insecurity.ts:55` calls `jws.verify(token, publicKey)` with no algorithm whitelist argument. `jws.verify` honours the alg header field supplied by the caller, so a token whose header declares alg of none (and an empty signature segment) is accepted as valid.
2. An attacker base64-encodes a header of {"alg":"none","typ":"JWT"} plus a payload of {data:{role:'admin'}} with an empty third segment; `verify()` returns true and `decode()` (`insecurity.ts:56`) yields the forged claims.
3. The jwtUnsignedChallenge in `routes/verify.ts:86` confirms this path is reachable.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: auth-identity - lib/insecurity.ts:55
    Attacker->>App: Crafted request exercising the weakness at lib/insecurity.ts line 55
    App->>App: Vulnerable branch executes without the missing control
    App-->>Attacker: Response confirms the weakness - CWE-347
    alt Current state — F-008
        Attacker->>App: Crafted request exploiting F-008 succeeds
        App-->>Attacker: Exploitation confirmed
    else After M-008 — Pin JWT verification to RS256 and reject alg:none in lib/ins
        Attacker->>App: Same request after the fix is applied
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-008](#m-008) (Pin JWT verification to RS256 and reject alg:none in lib/ins) lands, 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) is exploitable at `lib/insecurity.ts:55` (Critical-severity, [CWE-347](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/347.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-008](#m-008) (Pin JWT verification to RS256 and reject alg:none in `lib/insecurity.ts`)

### 3.5 Derived Password from OAuth Email Claim

**Source:** 🔴 [F-009](#f-009) — `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:30`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-287](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/287.html)). STRIDE: Spoofing. See [§7 F-009](#f-009) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. After an OAuth login, OAuthComponent derives the local account password deterministically from the email claim: `const password = btoa(profile.email.split('').reverse().join(''))` (`oauth.component.ts:30`), then both creates the user (line 31) and logs in (line 46) with that same value.
2. The password is therefore a pure function of a publicly-known identifier - base64 of the reversed email.
3. Any attacker who knows a victim's email can reproduce the exact password offline and authenticate through the normal password endpoint, turning the OAuth convenience feature into a parallel authentication bypass for every OAuth-provisioned account.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: frontend-spa - frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:30
    Attacker->>App: Crafted request exercising the weakness at frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts line 30
    App->>App: Vulnerable branch executes without the missing control
    App-->>Attacker: Response confirms the weakness - CWE-287
    alt Current state — F-009
        Attacker->>App: Crafted request exploiting F-009 succeeds
        App-->>Attacker: Exploitation confirmed
    else After M-009 — Stop deriving passwords from the email claim, provision OAut
        Attacker->>App: Same request after the fix is applied
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-009](#m-009) (Stop deriving passwords from the email claim; provision OAut) lands, 🔴 [F-009](#f-009) is exploitable at `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:30` (Critical-severity, [CWE-287](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/287.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-009](#m-009) (Stop deriving passwords from the email claim; provision OAuth accounts without a guessable password)

### 3.6 Insecure Direct Object Reference

**Source:** 🔴 [F-010](#f-010) — `routes/dataExport.ts:26`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-639](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/639.html)). STRIDE: Tampering. See [§7 F-010](#f-010) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. Server-side authorization MUST derive the resource owner from the authenticated session (`req.user` / `req.session` / `req.auth`), never from attacker-controlled request data.
2. Trusting `req.body.UserId` etc. enables horizontal privilege escalation across all authenticated tenants.
3. Send the crafted payload to the endpoint backed by `routes/dataExport.ts:26`.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
        Attacker->>App: Crafted request exploiting F-010 succeeds
        App-->>Attacker: Exploitation confirmed
    else After M-010 — Replace req.body.UserId/userId/ownerId with req.user.id (or
        Attacker->>App: Same request after the fix is applied
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-010](#m-010) (Replace `req.body.UserId`/userId/ownerId with `req.user.id` (or ) lands, 🔴 [F-010](#f-010) is exploitable at `routes/dataExport.ts:26` (Critical-severity, [CWE-639](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/639.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-010](#m-010) (Replace `req.body.UserId`/userId/ownerId with `req.user.id` (or equivalent session-derived identity) in every WHERE/filter clause.)

### 3.7 Unsalted MD5 password storage

**Source:** 🔴 [F-011](#f-011) — `models/user.ts:76`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-916](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/916.html)). STRIDE: Information Disclosure. See [§7 F-011](#f-011) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. The User model's password setter calls `security.hash()` (`models/user.ts:76`), which is defined as `crypto.createHash('md5').update`(data).digest('hex') with no salt and no work factor (`lib/insecurity.ts:41`).
2. Every account password - including the seeded admin - lands in the Users table as a bare 32-hex MD5 digest.
3. An attacker who reads the SQLite file via the SQL-injection paths in login/search, a stolen backup, or container filesystem access recovers the cleartext for common and even moderately complex passwords in seconds using GPU rainbow tables or hashcat mode 0.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: data-persistence - models/user.ts:76
    Attacker->>Attacker: Craft JWT with header alg=none and admin claims
    Attacker->>App: Crafted HTTP request to the affected endpoint with the unsigned token in Authorization
    App->>App: Validate token without pinning the signing algorithm
    App-->>Attacker: 200 OK - request authorised under forged admin identity
    alt Current state — F-011
        Attacker->>App: Crafted request exploiting F-011 succeeds
        App-->>Attacker: Exploitation confirmed
    else After M-011 — Replace MD5 password hashing with per-user salted bcrypt/arg
        Attacker->>App: Same request after the fix is applied
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-011](#m-011) (Replace MD5 password hashing with per-user salted bcrypt/arg) lands, 🔴 [F-011](#f-011) is exploitable at `models/user.ts:76` (Critical-severity, [CWE-916](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/916.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-011](#m-011) (Replace MD5 password hashing with per-user salted bcrypt/argon2 in the User model setter)

### 3.8 XML External Entity Injection

**Source:** 🔴 [F-012](#f-012) — `lib/xml.ts:35`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-611](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/611.html)). STRIDE: Information Disclosure. See [§7 F-012](#f-012) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. POST /file-upload accepts a .xml part and routes it to handleXmlUpload (`routes/fileUpload.ts:70`), which calls parseXmlString (`lib/xml.ts:33`).
2. The parser is configured with `XML_PARSE_NOENT` | `XML_PARSE_DTDLOAD` (`lib/xml.ts:35`) and explicitly registers host filesystem input providers via xmlRegisterFsInputProviders (`lib/xml.ts:21`), so a DOCTYPE declaring <!ENTITY xxe SYSTEM "file:///etc/passwd"> is resolved and the expanded entity is reflected back to the client in the 410 error body (`routes/fileUpload.ts:79`, `utils.trunc(xmlString, 400)`).
3. The route has no `isAuthorized()` guard (`server.ts:309`), so an anonymous attacker reads arbitrary server files and can pivot to internal URLs through SYSTEM entities.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant App
    Note over App: file-upload-handler - lib/xml.ts:35
    Attacker->>App: Crafted request exercising the weakness at lib/xml.ts line 35
    App->>App: Vulnerable branch executes without the missing control
    App-->>Attacker: Response confirms the weakness - CWE-611
    alt Current state — F-012
        Attacker->>App: Crafted request exploiting F-012 succeeds
        App-->>Attacker: Exploitation confirmed
    else After M-012 — Disable DTD loading and external-entity resolution in parseX
        Attacker->>App: Same request after the fix is applied
        App-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-012](#m-012) (Disable DTD loading and external-entity resolution in parseX) lands, 🔴 [F-012](#f-012) is exploitable at `lib/xml.ts:35` (Critical-severity, [CWE-611](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/611.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-012](#m-012) (Disable DTD loading and external-entity resolution in parseXmlString)

### 3.9 Server-Side Code Evaluation of Untrusted Input

**Source:** 🔴 [F-013](#f-013) — `routes/b2bOrder.ts:23`

Severity **Critical** ([CWE-94](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/94.html)). STRIDE: Elevation of Privilege. See [§7 F-013](#f-013) for the full register row.

**Attack Steps**

1. POST /b2b/v2/orders reads `body.orderLinesData` (`routes/b2bOrder.ts:19`) and at line 23 runs `vm.runInContext('safeEval(orderLinesData)', sandbox, { timeout: 2000 })`.
2. The string is evaluated as JavaScript by notevil's `safeEval`. notevil ^1.3.3 (`package.json:139`) is an interpreter-based sandbox with known escape primitives: a payload that walks `constructor` / `__proto__` chains reaches the real `Function`/`process` and executes host code.
3. An authenticated B2B client sends a crafted orderLinesData (`e.g`. an expression that reaches `this.constructor.constructor('return process')().mainModule.require('child_process').execSync(…)`) and obtains command execution on the Node process.

**Sequence Diagram**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    autonumber
    actor Attacker
    participant API
    participant Sandbox
    Note over API: b2b-api - routes/b2bOrder.ts:23
    Note over Sandbox: Eval / VM context
    Attacker->>API: POST /b2b/v2/orders with JS payload escaping the sandbox
    API->>Sandbox: Pass attacker-controlled code to eval / vm.runInContext
    Sandbox->>Sandbox: Prototype-walk reaches the host realm - RCE
    API-->>Attacker: Command output / arbitrary side effects
    alt Current state — F-013
        Attacker->>API: Crafted request exploiting F-013 succeeds
        API-->>Attacker: Exploitation confirmed
    else After M-013 — Replace safeEval/vm evaluation of orderLinesData with a decl
        Attacker->>API: Same request after the fix is applied
        API-->>Attacker: Request rejected
    end
```

**Key takeaway:** Until <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-013](#m-013) (Replace safeEval/vm evaluation of orderLinesData with a decl) lands, 🔴 [F-013](#f-013) is exploitable at `routes/b2bOrder.ts:23` (Critical-severity, [CWE-94](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/94.html)).

**Defense in Depth**

- Primary mitigation: <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-013](#m-013) (Replace safeEval/vm evaluation of orderLinesData with a declarative JSON parser and schema validation)

Information assets and the classification level that drives the Confidentiality / Integrity / Availability targets used in [§7 Findings Register](#7-findings-register) risk scoring.

| Asset | ID | Classification | Description |
|----------------------|-----|--------------|------------------------------------|
| User Credentials (Password Hashes) | A-001 | Restricted | User account passwords stored as unsalted<br/>MD5 hashes in the SQLite Users table<br/>(`lib/insecurity.ts:41`). Trivially crackable<br/>offline if the database is breached via SQL<br/>injection. |
| JWT Signing Private Key | A-002 | Restricted | RSA private key used to sign all session<br/>JWTs, hardcoded as a string literal in<br/>`lib/insecurity.ts:21` and committed to the<br/>public repository. Possession allows offline<br/>forgery of arbitrary admin tokens. |
| Payment Card & Wallet Data | A-004 | Restricted | Stored credit-card records (Card model) and<br/>wallet balances (Wallet model) associated<br/>with user accounts. Ownership enforcement<br/>relies on client-supplied UserId, creating<br/>IDOR exposure. |
| SQLite Database File | A-007 | Restricted | Embedded SQLite datastore co-located<br/>in-process with the application. Holds all<br/>persistent data; reachable in full via the<br/>intentional SQL injection paths in login and<br/>product search. |
| LLM Provider API Key | A-009 | Restricted | Credential for the OpenAI-compatible chatbot<br/>provider consumed by `routes/chat.ts` via<br/>@ai-sdk/openai-compatible. Compromise<br/>enables provider billing abuse and<br/>completion tampering. |
| CI/CD Secrets & GitHub Token | A-010 | Restricted | `GITHUB_TOKEN` and workflow secrets used by<br/>GitHub Actions. Exposed to over-broad scopes<br/>by missing permissions blocks and unpinned<br/>third-party actions in .github/workflows. |
| Session JWT Tokens | A-003 | Confidential | Bearer JWTs carrying user id and role,<br/>issued on login and stored in browser<br/>localStorage and a cookie. XSS-extractable;<br/>not revocable until expiry. |
| User PII (Email, Profile, Addresses) | A-005 | Confidential | Personally identifiable information: email<br/>addresses (plaintext, enumerable via login),<br/>security answers, delivery addresses, and<br/>profile data across the User and Address<br/>models. |
| Order, Basket & Complaint Data | A-006 | Confidential | User-owned business objects - baskets,<br/>basket items, orders, deliveries,<br/>complaints, feedback - accessible through<br/>routes whose ownership checks are<br/>inconsistently applied (BOLA/IDOR). |
| Uploaded Files & FTP Directory | A-008 | Internal | User-uploaded complaint attachments and<br/>profile images written into served<br/>directories (uploads/, ftp/). Exposed via<br/>the /ftp and /file-serve directory-traversal<br/>surface and the file-parser sandbox. |
| Application Source Code & Challenge<br/>Solutions | A-011 | Internal | TypeScript/Angular source, challenge<br/>metadata (`data/static/challenges.yml`), and<br/>code-fix snippets. Public repository -<br/>readable by anyone and accepting external<br/>pull requests into trunk. |
| Public Product Catalog & Content | A-012 | Public | Product listings, challenge listings,<br/>languages, and static assets served without<br/>authentication. No confidentiality<br/>requirement; integrity matters for trust. |

| DELETE | `/api/Quantitys/:id` | - | handler: `server.ts:429`<br/>_⚑ Review: no authz guard detected_ |
| GET | `/api/Recycles/:id` | - | handler: `server.ts:388`<br/>_⚑ Review: no authz guard detected_ |
| PUT | `/api/Recycles/:id` | - | handler: `server.ts:389`<br/>_⚑ Review: no authz guard detected_ |
| DELETE | `/api/Recycles/:id` | - | handler: `server.ts:390`<br/>_⚑ Review: no authz guard detected_ |
| POST | `/rest/2fa/disable` | - | handler: `server.ts:471`<br/>_⚑ Review: auth/token endpoint_ |
| POST | `/rest/2fa/setup` | - | handler: `server.ts:465`<br/>_⚑ Review: auth/token endpoint_ |
| GET | `/rest/2fa/status` | - | handler: `server.ts:463`<br/>_⚑ Review: auth/token endpoint_ |
| GET | `/rest/basket/:id` | - | GET /rest/basket/:id - BOLA: basket id supplied by client<br/>_⚑ Review: no authz guard detected_ |
| POST | `/rest/basket/:id/checkout` | - | handler: `server.ts:604`<br/>_⚑ Review: no authz guard detected_ |
| PUT | `/​rest/​basket/​:​id/​coupon/​:​coupon` | - | handler: `server.ts:605`<br/>_⚑ Review: no authz guard detected_ |
| GET | `/rest/products/:id/reviews` | - | handler: `server.ts:632`<br/>_⚑ Review: no authz guard detected_ |
| PUT | `/rest/products/:id/reviews` | - | handler: `server.ts:633`<br/>_⚑ Review: no authz guard detected_ |

_25 further entry point(s) in this category carry no linked finding and no elevated review signal, and are not listed individually (52 total). The complete route inventory is available in `.route-inventory.json` and, when exported, `pentest-tasks.yaml`._

---

## 6. Security Architecture

This chapter is organized by security-control category. The architecture section avoids artificial control IDs and finding-ID columns in overview tables. Findings are listed only where the affected control is described.

_[§6](#6-security-architecture) schema v2 (13-section control-category layout). Cataloged controls: 31 total - 1 adequate, 7 partial, 8 weak, 10 unsafe, 5 missing. Linked threats: 70._

**How to read the verdicts.** Every control category (and every sub-control below it) carries exactly one status. The two red verdicts do **not** mean the same thing - this is the distinction that decides what you have to do about a finding:

| Status | Meaning | What it asks of you |
|----------|------------------------------------|------------------------|
| 🟢 Adequate | Control is present and sound | Nothing - keep it |
| 🟡 Partial | Present, but with meaningful gaps | Close the gap |
| 🟠 Weak | Present, but has exploitable gaps | Strengthen it |
| 🔴 Unsafe | **Present and relied upon, but defeated /<br/>trivially bypassable** | **Fix the existing control** |
| 🔴 Missing | **Control was never built** | **Add the control** |
| - | Not applicable to this codebase | - |

So "🔴 Unsafe" on a control category does *not* mean the control is absent - it means the control exists but does not hold (`e.g`. an MD5 password hash, a raw-SQL query path, a hardcoded signing key). "🔴 Missing" is reserved for controls that were never built (`e.g`. no Content-Security-Policy header).

### 6.1 Security Control Overview

|----------------------|---------|------------------------------------|

| [6.3 Session and Token Controls](#63-session-and-token-controls) | 🔴 Unsafe | 3 routed findings; catalogued controls are<br/>present but defeated (`e.g`. Session Token<br/>Signing (JWT Based), Session Token<br/>Validation (JWT Based)). |

### 6.2 Identity and Authentication Controls

**Verdict:** 🔴 Unsafe

<!-- The line below is mechanically derived from the controls table — LLM must not re-author it. -->
**Controls covered:**

- [7.2.1 Threat Hypotheses Requiring Validation](#threat-hypotheses-requiring-validation)
- [7.2.2 Password-Based Authentication](#password-based-authentication)
- [7.2.3 Multi-Factor Authentication](#multi-factor-authentication)
- [7.2.4 OAuth / Federated Login](#oauth-federated-login)

**Implemented controls:** TOTP-based 2FA enrollment and verification (when opted in), OAuth frontend identity adapter via `oauth.component.ts`, Angular route guards (`LoginGuard`, `AdminGuard`) for UI-layer gating, express-rate-limit applied to `/rest/user/reset-password` and 2FA routes.

**Assessment:** The credential verification path (`routes/login.ts`) and the OAuth adapter (`oauth.component.ts`) are both fully implemented and actively used, but each is defeated by a different mechanism: the login path is injectable via raw SQL interpolation (🔴 [F-001](#f-001)), the OAuth path derives a deterministic local password from the user's email address (🔴 [F-009](#f-009)), and the JWT issuance that follows every successful flow is signed with a key committed to the public repository (🔴 [F-007](#f-007)). None of the client-side Angular guards constitute a security boundary - they read a client-decoded token that the server does not consistently re-verify on every call (🟠 [F-006](#f-006), 🔴 [F-050](#f-050)). Each successful flow above terminates in the server issuing a session token; the signing, validation, propagation, storage, and lifecycle of that token are described in [§6.3 Session and Token Controls](#63-session-and-token-controls).

<!-- §6.2 AUTH-MECHANISMS-FROZEN — deterministic inventory, pregenerator-owned. DO NOT EDIT. -->
**Authentication mechanisms (at a glance).** Every authentication mechanism detected on the application, its effective status, where it is assessed, and its linked findings. Controls are catalogued by domain, so JWT/session handling is assessed under [§6.3 Session and Token Controls](#63-session-and-token-controls) and password hashing under [§6.9 Cryptography Secrets and Data Protection](#69-cryptography-secrets-and-data-protection).

| Mechanism | Status | Assessed in | Findings |
|----------------------|----------|-----------|------------------------------------------------|
| User registration | 🔴 Critical | [§6.2](#62-identity-and-authentication-controls) | 🔴 [F-002](#f-002) — Systemic Mass Assignment of Privileged Fields<br/>🔴 [F-005](#f-005) — Sensitive Routes Registered Without Authorization (`server.ts`) |
| Password login | 🔴 Unsafe | [§6.2](#62-identity-and-authentication-controls) | 🟠 [F-014](#f-014) — Missing Brute-Force Protection on Login |
| Password reset / change | 🟠 High | [§6.2](#62-identity-and-authentication-controls) | 🟠 [F-016](#f-016) — Knowledge-Based Password Reset Without Token |
| Password storage (hashing) | 🔴 Unsafe | [§6.9](#69-cryptography-secrets-and-data-protection) | 🔴 [F-011](#f-011) — Unsalted MD5 password storage |
| JWT / bearer-token session | 🔴 Unsafe | [§6.3](#63-session-and-token-controls) | 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — Insecure JWT Verification<br/>🔴 [F-046](#f-046) — Insecure Client-Side Storage of JWT in localStorage<br/>🟡 [F-054](#f-054) — No JWT Revocation or Session Invalidation<br/>🔴 [F-057](#f-057) — Hardcoded HMAC Key Enables Deluxe-Token Forgery |
| Session-token storage | 🔴 Unsafe | [§6.3](#63-session-and-token-controls) | 🔴 [F-046](#f-046) — Insecure Client-Side Storage of JWT in localStorage<br/>🟠 [F-047](#f-047) — Session Token Stored in Non-HttpOnly Cookie |
| Multi-factor authentication (TOTP / 2FA) | 🟡 Partial | [§6.2](#62-identity-and-authentication-controls) | 🔴 [F-015](#f-015) — Weak 2FA Token Signing Key |
| OAuth / OIDC federated login | 🔴 Unsafe | [§6.2](#62-identity-and-authentication-controls) | 🔴 [F-009](#f-009) — Derived Password from OAuth Email Claim<br/>🟠 [F-019](#f-019) — Untrusted URL-Fragment Parsing of OAuth Token<br/>🟠 [F-020](#f-020) — OAuth Implicit Flow / Token in URL Fragment |
