<a id="t-044"></a><a id="f-044"></a>
#### F-044 · Payment card number stored cleartext

**Severity:** 🟠 High _(raw Critical)_  ·  **Component:** [C-04](#c-04) - Data Persistence Layer  ·  **Location:** `models/card.ts:38`

**Issue:** The Card model declares cardNum as a plain DataTypes.INTEGER with only numeric range validators (`models/card.ts:38-45`) and fullName as a plain STRING (line 37); no setter encrypts either value before persistence. A grep of models/ and `data/datacreator.ts` for any encrypt/cipher/aes/crypto usage returns zero hits, so the declared 'encrypted Card field' control does not exist in code.

Cardholder PAN and name are written to the Cards table in cleartext. Stored PANs are recoverable in cleartext from a single database read, a direct PCI-DSS cardholder-data exposure.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `models/card.ts:38-45` defines cardNum as a bare INTEGER with no encrypting setter; no encryption primitive is referenced anywhere in models/ or data/datacreator.ts.

**Fix:** Encrypt the data in transit and at rest with vetted primitives → <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-044](#m-044) — Encrypt or tokenize stored card numbers with an application-level AEAD setter on the Card model (`card.ts:38`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-311](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/311.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-045"></a><a id="f-045"></a>
#### F-045 · Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-05](#c-05) - File Upload & Parser Subsystem  ·  **Location:** `routes/profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`

**Issue:** POST /profile/image/url passes `req.body.imageUrl` directly into fetch(url) with no scheme, host, or IP allowlist. An authenticated user submits imageUrl=http://169.254.169.254/latest/meta-data/ or http://localhost:3000/internal to make the server issue the request from inside the trust boundary.

The response body is streamed to disk under the user's profile-image path (line 29); on any fetch error the raw attacker URL is instead stored verbatim as profileImage (line 36), enabling a stored payload. Authenticated attacker reads cloud-metadata credentials and probes/contacts internal-only services that trust the application's network origin.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `req.body.imageUrl` reaches `fetch()` unfiltered at `profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`; the only gate is that a session cookie maps to a logged-in user.

**Fix:** Validate the URL scheme + host against an explicit allow-list before issuing outbound requests → <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-045](#m-045) — Validate imageUrl against an allowlist and block internal/link-local targets before fetch (`profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`)

**Classification:** Server-Side Request Forgery · [CWE-918](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/918.html) · [OWASP A10:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A10_2021/)

<a id="t-046"></a><a id="f-046"></a>
#### F-046 · Insecure Storage of Sensitive Information

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular Single-Page Application  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:51`

**Issue:** The session JWT is persisted in `localStorage` (`oauth.component.ts:51` `localStorage.setItem('token', authentication.token)`; read back by the guards at `app.guard.ts:18` and :35). localStorage is readable by any JavaScript executing in the origin, so any of the confirmed XSS sinks in this SPA (`search-result.component.ts:143` DOM XSS, `data-export.component.ts:71` `document.write`, the bypassSecurityTrustHtml sinks) can exfiltrate the bearer token in a single line, granting full session hijack.

The token is also long-lived (the OAuth flow copies it into an 8-hour cookie at `oauth.component.ts:48-50`) and survives tab/window close. Any XSS in the origin yields immediate session-token theft and account takeover with no additional user interaction.

**Root cause:** Attacker-controlled content is rendered in the victim's browser without sanitization; combined with session tokens held in JavaScript-readable storage, any payload yields immediate account takeover.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `oauth.component.ts:51` writes the JWT to localStorage and `app.guard.ts:18`/:35 reads it back; no HttpOnly/CSP boundary protects it from JavaScript.

**Fix:** <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-046](#m-046) — Move the session token out of localStorage into an HttpOnly Secure SameSite cookie via a BFF (`oauth.component.ts:51`)

**Classification:** Insecure Client-Side Storage · [CWE-922](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/922.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-047"></a><a id="f-047"></a>
#### F-047 · Sensitive Cookie without HttpOnly

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular Single-Page Application  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:50`

**Issue:** OAuthComponent writes the session token into a cookie via the client-side `ngy-cookie` library: `this.cookieService.put('token', authentication.token, { expires })` (`oauth.component.ts:50`). A cookie set from JavaScript cannot carry the HttpOnly flag, and the call sets neither Secure nor SameSite.

The token is therefore both JavaScript-readable (XSS-extractable, same blast radius as the localStorage copy) and, lacking Secure, transmissible over any cleartext request to the origin. Token theft via XSS and exposure on cleartext channels; cookie cannot be hardened while set client-side.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `oauth.component.ts:50` sets the `token` cookie through ngy-cookie with only `expires` - no HttpOnly (impossible from JS), no Secure, no SameSite.

**Fix:** Set `HttpOnly` on every session cookie → <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-047](#m-047) — Set the session cookie server-side with HttpOnly, Secure and SameSite=Strict (`oauth.component.ts:50`)

**Classification:** Insecure Client-Side Storage · [CWE-1004](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1004.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-048"></a><a id="f-048"></a>
#### F-048 · Information Disclosure

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-08](#c-08) - Socket\.IO Real-Time Channel  ·  **Location:** `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:30`

**Issue:** On every new connection the handler replays the entire shared `notifications` array to the connecting socket: `notifications.forEach((notification) => socket.emit('challenge solved', notification))` at lines 29-31. Each notification object built in `challengeUtils.ts:62-69` includes a `flag` field - the CTF flag produced by `utils.ctfFlag(challenge.name)`, the secret value that proves a challenge was solved.

Combined with finding -001 (no connection auth), an anonymous attacker connects and immediately receives the flags of every challenge any user has solved this session, without solving the challenges. Anonymous clients harvest CTF flags (the proof-of-solve secrets) for all solved challenges without authentication or solving them.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `registerWebsocketEvents.ts:30` emits each `notifications[]` entry - which carries a `flag` field - to every connecting socket, and `challengeUtils.ts:75` broadcasts the same flag-bearing object to all sockets.

**Fix:** Restrict the response to the minimum fields needed and never echo secrets → <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-048](#m-048) — Strip the flag field from challenge-solved notifications before emitting and gate replay by authenticated principal (`registerWebsocketEvents.ts:30`)

**Classification:** Insecure Real-Time Channel · [CWE-200](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/200.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-049"></a><a id="f-049"></a>
#### F-049 · Missing Rate Limiting (Brute-Force)

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Monolith  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:346`

**Issue:** The reset-password rate limiter's keyGenerator returns headers['X-Forwarded-For'] ?? ip, and trust proxy is enabled.

Because X-Forwarded-For is fully attacker-controlled, an attacker rotates the header per request to land in a fresh bucket each time, defeating the 100-per-5-minutes cap and enabling unlimited password-reset brute force (the resetPasswordMortyChallenge). Rate limiting on the password-reset flow is fully bypassable, enabling brute force of security answers.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - keyGenerator reads headers['X-Forwarded-For'] directly as the limiter key with trust proxy enabled.

**Fix:** Apply rate limiting and lock-out thresholds on authentication endpoints → <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-049](#m-049) — Key rate limiters on the validated proxy-derived client IP (`server.ts:346`)

**Classification:** Denial of Service · [CWE-307](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/307.html) · [OWASP A04:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A04_2021/)

<a id="t-050"></a><a id="f-050"></a>
#### F-050 · Improper Authorization

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Authentication & Identity Subsystem  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:156`

**Issue:** `isAccounting()` (`insecurity.ts:156`), `isDeluxe()` (`insecurity.ts:166`), and `isCustomer()` (`insecurity.ts:171`) gate access using decode(jwtFrom(req)).data.role after the broken `verify()` (🔴 [F-008](#f-008)). The pattern verify(token) && decode(token) returns false-on-failure but, because verify accepts alg:none and the signing key is public, the decoded role claim is fully attacker-controlled.

An attacker presents a forged token with `data.role` of 'accounting' to reach accounting-only endpoints (`e.g`. order management), or 'admin' elsewhere, escalating from any authenticated context to privileged roles.

An attacker assigns themselves any role in a forged token and reaches accounting/admin-gated functionality.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - Role-based authorization at `insecurity.ts:156-173` trusts the decoded role claim from a token validated by the alg:none-vulnerable `verify()`, making the privilege gate attacker-controlled.

**Fix:** Add explicit server-side authorisation checks on every protected route → <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-050](#m-050) — Verify tokens with a pinned algorithm and resolve roles from the trusted user record (`insecurity.ts:156`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-285](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/285.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-051"></a><a id="f-051"></a>
#### F-051 · Improper Authorization

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - AI Chatbot Service  ·  **Location:** `routes/chat.ts:176`

**Issue:** LLM06 - Excessive Agency: the chatbot is wired with four tools (`searchProducts`, `getProductReviews`, `getOrderById`, `generateCoupon`) at `routes/chat.ts:116-187` that the model invokes autonomously with no human-in-the-loop approval and no server-side authorization gate keyed to the action's sensitivity. `generateCoupon` (line 176) is a state-changing, financially significant action whose only constraint is the natural-language coupon policy in the system prompt - the model decides both whether to call it and what `discount` to pass (line 179).

Because the decision authority is delegated entirely to a component that is itself steerable by untrusted chat input, any successful prompt manipulation is an immediate privilege escalation from 'customer asking a question' to 'customer issuing themselves discounts'. The model can be coerced into performing a privileged financial action no unauthenticated/normal user is authorized to perform directly.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - generateCoupon is a financial write tool exposed to an autonomous model with no approval step or server-side eligibility check before execution.

**Fix:** Add explicit server-side authorisation checks on every protected route → <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-051](#m-051) — Gate sensitive LLM tools behind server-side authorization and least-privilege scope (`chat.ts:176`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-285](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/285.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-052"></a><a id="f-052"></a>
#### F-052 · Improper Authorization

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-09](#c-09) - CI/CD & Source-Contribution Integrity  ·  **Location:** `.github/workflows/ci.yml:1`

**Issue:** Of the 16 workflows, only `lock.yml` and `pr-compliance.yml` declare a top-level `permissions:` block; the other 14 (`ci.yml`, `release.yml`, `image_actions.yml`, `zap_scan.yml`, `lint-fixer.yml`, the update-* family, `stale.yml`, `rebase.yml`, `frontend-bundle-analysis.yml`) declare none at the workflow level. Without an explicit block the job inherits the repository default `GITHUB_TOKEN` scope, which for many older repo settings is read/write across contents, packages, pull-requests, issues, and more.

Every step in those workflows - including the unpinned/third-party actions in `image_actions.yml` and `ci.yml`, and any postinstall code that runs on PRs (see 🟠 [F-030](#f-030)) - then operates with a far broader token than its task needs. Any compromised step inside a permission-unscoped workflow wields a broad read/write `GITHUB_TOKEN`, enabling repository tampering, package publication, or PR manipulation well beyond the step's legitimate need.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - 14 of 16 workflow files (`e.g`. `ci.yml`, `release.yml`, `image_actions.yml`) declare no top-level permissions block, so `GITHUB_TOKEN` defaults to the repository-wide scope instead of the least-privilege model `codeql-analysis.yml:11-14` demonstrates.

**Fix:** Add explicit server-side authorisation checks on every protected route → <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-052](#m-052) — Add least-privilege permissions blocks to all 14 unscoped workflows (default contents: read) (`ci.yml:1`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-285](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/285.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-053"></a><a id="f-053"></a>
#### F-053 · Improper Access Control

**Severity:** 🟠 High  ·  **Component:** [C-04](#c-04) - Data Persistence Layer  ·  **Location:** `models/index.ts:41`

**Issue:** `models/index.ts:33-43` instantiates a single Sequelize/SQLite connection backed by the file data/juiceshop.sqlite, co-located in-process with all application logic and using one undifferentiated DB principal ('username'/'password' placeholders, no row-level or schema-level privilege separation). There is no network boundary, no least-privilege DB user, and no separation between the Users/Cards tables and lower-sensitivity tables.

Consequently any SQL-injection foothold reaching this connection - `e.g`. the raw template-string login and search queries that bypass the ORM - reads and writes every table, including password hashes and card data, with no further containment.

A single injection or in-process compromise yields read/write over the entire datastore - credentials, cards, and orders alike - with no privilege boundary.

**Root cause:** Authorization checks are absent or bypassable, allowing horizontal and vertical privilege jumps from a self-registered or low-rights account. Includes mass-assignment of privileged attributes.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `models/index.ts:33-43` wires one in-process SQLite connection with a single all-powerful DB principal and a co-located file store, so any injected query reaches all tables.

**Fix:** Add explicit server-side authorisation checks on every protected route → <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-053](#m-053) — Introduce least-privilege and isolation for the datastore to limit blast radius of injection (`index.ts:41`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-284](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/284.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

### 🟡 Medium (17)

<a id="t-054"></a><a id="f-054"></a>
#### F-054 · No Revocation Session Invalidation

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Authentication & Identity Subsystem  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:54`

**Issue:** `authorize()` (`insecurity.ts:54`) issues stateless RS256 tokens with a fixed 6h expiry and no jti, and `verify()` (`insecurity.ts:55`) only checks the signature. The authenticatedUsers map (`insecurity.ts:70`) is an in-memory cache, not a revocation list, and updateAuthenticatedUsers (`insecurity.ts:189`) re-adds any validly signed token it sees.

A stolen token cannot be revoked before its 6h expiry, so account compromise persists through password changes and logout.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - Tokens are pure stateless JWTs with no jti or server-side revocation list; the authenticatedUsers map self-populates from any valid signature at `insecurity.ts`:189.

**Fix:** <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-054](#m-054) — Add a server-side token revocation list keyed on jti (`insecurity.ts:54`)

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-613](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/613.html) · [OWASP A07:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A07_2021/)

<a id="t-055"></a><a id="f-055"></a>
#### F-055 · Insufficient Verification of Data Authenticity

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-10](#c-10) - Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface  ·  **Location:** `routes/web3Wallet.ts:15`

**Issue:** POST /rest/web3/walletExploitAddress reads `req.body.walletAddress` and immediately does `walletsConnected.add`(metamaskAddress) with no ownership proof. The ContractExploited on-chain event handler (`routes/web3Wallet.ts:26`) then solves `challenges.web3WalletChallenge` for any exploiter address present in walletsConnected.

Callers assert arbitrary wallet addresses as their own, spoofing on-chain exploit attribution and the resulting challenge solve.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - contractExploitListener adds the raw request-body address to walletsConnected before any verification, and the event handler honors that set without re-checking caller identity.

**Fix:** <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-055](#m-055) — Bind walletExploitAddress entries to a signed wallet proof and session (`web3Wallet.ts:15`)

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-345](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/345.html) · [OWASP A07:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A07_2021/)

<a id="t-056"></a><a id="f-056"></a>
#### F-056 · Origin Validation Error

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-08](#c-08) - Socket\.IO Real-Time Channel  ·  **Location:** `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:20`

**Issue:** The server CORS config at line 20 pins `origin: 'http://localhost:4200'` - the local dev frontend. In the deployed container the real frontend is served same-origin on port 3000, so this hardcoded dev origin does not match production and the value provides no meaningful production allowlist.

Cross-origin pages and non-browser clients reach the channel because origin is neither correctly configured for production nor validated server-side.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `registerWebsocketEvents.ts:20` hardcodes a dev-only CORS origin and no handler validates `socket.handshake.headers.origin`; CORS is the only origin-related control present.

**Fix:** <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-056](#m-056) — Configure the production CORS origin allowlist and validate handshake origin server-side (`registerWebsocketEvents.ts:20`)

**Classification:** Cross-Site Request Forgery (CSRF) · [CWE-346](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/346.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-057"></a><a id="f-057"></a>
#### F-057 · Hardcoded Credentials

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Authentication & Identity Subsystem  ·  **Location:** `lib/insecurity.ts:150`

**Issue:** `deluxeToken()` derives a membership token via crypto.createHmac('sha256', privateKey).update(email + 'deluxe'). The HMAC key is the same leaked RSA private-key literal from `insecurity.ts:21`, which is public.

Any authenticated user forges a valid deluxe-membership token, obtaining paid entitlements without payment.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - deluxeToken at `insecurity.ts:150` HMACs with the public privateKey literal, so the entitlement token is attacker-computable from a known email.

**Fix:** Move the credential out of source control into a secret store and rotate it → <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-057](#m-057) — Derive entitlement tokens from a secret-managed key distinct from the JWT key (`insecurity.ts:150`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-798](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/798.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-058"></a><a id="f-058"></a>
#### F-058 · Insufficient Verification of Data Authenticity

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-09](#c-09) - CI/CD & Source-Contribution Integrity  ·  **Location:** `.github/workflows/release.yml:73`

**Issue:** The `release.yml` docker job (lines 73-85) and the `ci.yml` docker job (lines 337-349) build and push `bkimminich/juice-shop` images to Docker Hub without generating a signature or a provenance/SBOM attestation that consumers can verify. The Dockerfile does run `npm run sbom` (Dockerfile:20) to embed a CycloneDX SBOM inside the image, but the published image itself is neither cosign-signed nor accompanied by a SLSA provenance statement, and `softprops/action-gh-release` (`release.yml:46`) attaches the packaged tarballs to the GitHub release with no detached signature.

Downstream operators cannot verify image authenticity, so a Docker Hub push-credential compromise or registry substitution goes undetected and propagates to every consumer of the latest tag.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `release.yml:73-85` and `ci.yml:337-349` push container images and `release.yml:45-49` attaches release tarballs with no cosign signature or SLSA provenance attestation step anywhere in the publish path.

**Fix:** <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-058](#m-058) — Sign published images with cosign and emit SLSA provenance for releases (`release.yml:73`)

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-345](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/345.html) · [OWASP A06:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A06_2021/)

<a id="t-059"></a><a id="f-059"></a>
#### F-059 · Mutable Major-Version Action Tags CI

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-09](#c-09) - CI/CD & Source-Contribution Integrity  ·  **Location:** `.github/workflows/ci.yml:188`

**Issue:** While most actions in `ci.yml` and `release.yml` are SHA-pinned, several remain on mutable major-version tags that GitHub allows the publisher to retag at will: `coverallsapp/github-action@v2` (`ci.yml:188`), `github/codeql-action/init@v3` / `autobuild@v3` / `analyze@v3` (`codeql-analysis.yml:23`,34,36), and `actions/checkout@v6` (`image_actions.yml:30`). A publisher (or an attacker who takes over the publisher account) can move the `v2`/`v3` tag to a malicious commit; the next workflow run silently consumes it.

A retag of any mutable-tag action executes attacker code in CI with whatever token the step is handed, ranging from coverage-token leakage to `GITHUB_TOKEN` compromise.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `ci.yml:188` consumes coverallsapp/github-action@v2 on a mutable major tag and passes `GITHUB_TOKEN` to it (line 190), diverging from the SHA-pinning convention used for actions/checkout and setup-node in the same file.

**Fix:** <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-059](#m-059) — SHA-pin coverallsapp/github-action and codeql-action references to match repo convention (`ci.yml:188`)

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-1357](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1357.html) · [OWASP A06:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A06_2021/)

<a id="t-060"></a><a id="f-060"></a>
#### F-060 · Improper Restriction of UI Rendering Layers (Clickjacking)

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-01](#c-01) - Angular Single-Page Application  ·  **Location:** `frontend/src/index.html:8`

**Issue:** `index.html` ships no Content-Security-Policy (no meta CSP tag in the document head, lines 8-29) and loads third-party resources (Google Fonts CSS/Gstatic) without Subresource Integrity. With multiple confirmed XSS sinks in this SPA (`search-result.component.ts:143`, `data-export.component.ts:71`, the bypassSecurityTrustHtml family) and the session token sitting in JavaScript-readable storage, the absence of a CSP means an injected script has no restriction on inline execution or on the origins it may exfiltrate the stolen token to.

No containment for injected scripts: token exfiltration to arbitrary origins and inline script execution proceed unimpeded once any XSS fires.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `index.html` (head, lines 8-29) contains no Content-Security-Policy meta tag and loads remote font resources without integrity attributes.

**Fix:** Add a frame-ancestors directive to the Content Security Policy → <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-060](#m-060) — Add a Content-Security-Policy (preferably via server header) and SRI for third-party scripts (`index.html:8`)

**Classification:** Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) · [CWE-1021](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1021.html) · [OWASP A03:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A03_2021/)

<a id="t-061"></a><a id="f-061"></a>
#### F-061 · Insufficient Logging

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Monolith  ·  **Location:** `routes/login.ts:18`

**Instances (7):** 🟢 `routes/b2bOrder.ts:16`, 🟡 `routes/login.ts:18`, 🟢 `routes/chat.ts:181`, 🟢 `.github/workflows/lint-fixer.yml:22`, 🟡 `routes/fileUpload.ts:39`, 🟢 `routes/nftMint.ts:44`, 🟢 `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:23`

**Issue:** The login handler and the authorization layer record no structured security audit events: successful and failed logins, token issuance, role changes, B2B order evaluation, and admin actions are not logged with actor/action/resource/timestamp. morgan logs HTTP access lines only.

Inability to attribute or reconstruct account-takeover and privileged actions; actions are repudiable.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `login.ts` mints tokens with no audit-log call; the codebase relies on morgan HTTP logging with no security-event log.

**Fix:** <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-061](#m-061) — Emit structured security audit events for auth and privileged operations (`login.ts:18`)

**Classification:** Missing Audit Logging & Accountability · [CWE-778](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/778.html) · [OWASP A09:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A09_2021/)

<a id="t-062"></a><a id="f-062"></a>
#### F-062 · Information Disclosure

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Monolith  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:676`

**Issue:** GET /metrics is registered with no auth middleware (`server.ts:676` and again at 729) and serves the full Prometheus registry, including app_users_registered counts by customer type, file-upload metrics, and the LLM input/output token counters defined in `chat.ts`. An unauthenticated attacker scrapes /metrics to profile user-base size, business activity, and LLM usage/cost, and to fingerprint the deployment.

Operational and business telemetry (user counts, upload/LLM activity) disclosed to anyone.

**Root cause:** Confidential files, credentials, and management-plane endpoints are reachable on unauthenticated routes; SSRF lets the server fetch internal resources on the attacker's behalf; unsafe path-handling primitives leak server content.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `app.get('/metrics', serveMetrics())` has no `security.isAuthorized()` and serveMetrics returns `register.metrics()` verbatim.

**Fix:** Restrict the response to the minimum fields needed and never echo secrets → <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-062](#m-062) — Authenticate or network-restrict the /metrics endpoint (`server.ts:676`)

**Classification:** Error Information Disclosure · [CWE-200](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/200.html) · [OWASP A05:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A05_2021/)

<a id="t-063"></a><a id="f-063"></a>
#### F-063 · Client-Side-Only Access Control Tool-Call Debug

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-07](#c-07) - AI Chatbot Service  ·  **Location:** `routes/chat.ts:220`

**Issue:** Broken Access Control: the server unconditionally streams `tool-call` events - including internal tool names and serialized arguments - to every caller at `routes/chat.ts:220-238`, regardless of role. The only role logic in that branch (lines 221-226) merely solves the `aiDebuggingChallenge`; it does NOT gate emission of the data.

Non-admin users enumerate the chatbot's internal tool surface and argument values intended for admin debugging only.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - The backend streams internal tool-call names and arguments to all clients; the admin-only restriction exists only as a client-side cookie check, not a server-side authorization gate.

**Fix:** <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-063](#m-063) — Suppress tool-call debug frames server-side unless the caller is an admin (`chat.ts:220`)

**Classification:** Broken Access Control · [CWE-602](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/602.html) · [OWASP A01:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A01_2021/)

<a id="t-064"></a><a id="f-064"></a>
#### F-064 · Dockerfile directive (non-root)

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Monolith  ·  **Location:** `test/smoke/Dockerfile:1`

**Issue:** Dockerfile USER directive (non-root) in /home/mrohr/juice-shop/test/smoke/Dockerfile.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous

**Fix:** <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-064](#m-064) — Add USER <non-root-uid> (`Dockerfile:1`)

**Classification:** Error Information Disclosure · [CWE-250](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/250.html) · [OWASP A05:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A05_2021/)

<a id="t-065"></a><a id="f-065"></a>
#### F-065 · Improper Verification of Cryptographic Signature

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-09](#c-09) - CI/CD & Source-Contribution Integrity  ·  **Location:** `.github/workflows/stale.yml:1`

**Instances (16):** `.github/workflows/stale.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/rebase.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/codeql-analysis.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/image_actions.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/pr-compliance.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/zap_scan.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/update-challenges-www-legacy.yml:1`, `.github/workflows/update-news-www-legacy.yml:1` … (+8 more)

**Issue:** Container image signing via cosign or attest-build-provenance in /home/mrohr/juice-shop/.github/workflows/stale.yml.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous

**Fix:** Pin the signature algorithm explicitly and reject `alg:none` and unknown algorithms → <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-065](#m-065) — Add cosign signing step to release workflow; or use actions/attest-build-provenance (`stale.yml:1`)

**Classification:** Broken Authentication · [CWE-347](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/347.html) · [OWASP A07:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A07_2021/)

<a id="t-066"></a><a id="f-066"></a>
#### F-066 · Dockerfile npm/pnpm/yarn uses --ignore-scripts

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-02](#c-02) - Express REST API Monolith  ·  **Location:** `test/smoke/Dockerfile:1`

**Instances (2):** `test/smoke/Dockerfile:1`, `Dockerfile:1`

**Issue:** Dockerfile npm/pnpm/yarn uses --ignore-scripts in /home/mrohr/juice-shop/test/smoke/Dockerfile.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous

**Fix:** <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-066](#m-066) — Use `npm ci --ignore-scripts` and audit required postinstalls separately (`Dockerfile:1`)

**Classification:** Supply-Chain Integrity · [CWE-506](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/506.html) · [OWASP A06:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A06_2021/)

<a id="t-067"></a><a id="f-067"></a>
#### F-067 · Hardcoded Credentials

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-04](#c-04) - Data Persistence Layer  ·  **Location:** `models/securityAnswer.ts:45`

**Issue:** The SecurityAnswer model setter stores answers as `security.hmac(answer) (models/securityAnswer.ts:45),` where hmac is HMAC-SHA256 keyed with the literal string 'pa4qacea4VK9t9nGv7yZtwmj' hardcoded in `lib/insecurity.ts`:42. Because the key is in source and the same for every install, and because the HMAC is unsalted and deterministic, an attacker who reads the SecurityAnswers table (via the same DB-read avenues as the other findings) can precompute HMACs for likely answers - security questions draw from small answer spaces (pet names, cities, maiden names) - and recover the cleartext answers offline.

Security answers are recoverable via offline precomputation against a known key, enabling password-reset account takeover.

**Root cause:** Authentication can be circumvented or forged because credentials, signing keys, or password hashes are weak, missing, or exposed.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - `models/securityAnswer.ts:45` transforms each answer with `security.hmac()`, which `lib/insecurity.ts:42` keys with a hardcoded constant shared across all deployments.

**Fix:** Move the credential out of source control into a secret store and rotate it → <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-067](#m-067) — Hash security answers with a per-user salted adaptive function and a managed secret (`securityAnswer.ts:45`)

**Classification:** Cryptographic Failures · [CWE-798](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/798.html) · [OWASP A02:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A02_2021/)

<a id="t-068"></a><a id="f-068"></a>
#### F-068 · Allocation of Resources without Limits

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-03](#c-03) - Authentication & Identity Subsystem  ·  **Location:** `server.ts:346`

**Issue:** The reset-password rate limiter keys requests on headers['X-Forwarded-For'] ?? ip (`server.ts:346`). An attacker defeats the reset-password throttle by rotating a spoofed header, enabling high-volume security-answer brute force.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - The limiter's keyGenerator at `server.ts:346` trusts the client-supplied X-Forwarded-For header, so a new header value resets the per-key counter.

**Fix:** Bound the request rate and the per-request resource budget on this endpoint → <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-068](#m-068) — Key the reset-password rate limiter on a trusted client identifier (`server.ts:346`)

**Classification:** Denial of Service · [CWE-770](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/770.html) · [OWASP A04:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A04_2021/)

<a id="t-069"></a><a id="f-069"></a>
#### F-069 · Entity Expansion Denial Service

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-05](#c-05) - File Upload & Parser Subsystem  ·  **Location:** `routes/fileUpload.ts:76`

**Issue:** Because parseXmlString enables DTD loading and entity substitution (`lib/xml.ts:35`), a billion-laughs DOCTYPE (nested entities &lol9; referencing &lol8; etc.) submitted to POST /file-upload as .xml expands exponentially during libxml2 parsing. The application explicitly anticipates this: handleXmlUpload solves xxeDosChallenge when the error contains 'Script execution timed out' (`routes/fileUpload.ts:82-85`).

Concurrent crafted XML uploads pin CPU and stall the Node event loop, denying service to legitimate users.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - DTD/entity expansion is enabled in parseXmlString and the handler's catch block is purpose-built around the 'Script execution timed out' DoS outcome.

**Fix:** <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-069](#m-069) — Disable DTD/entity expansion and rate-limit XML uploads (`fileUpload.ts:76`)

**Classification:** Denial of Service · [CWE-776](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/776.html) · [OWASP A04:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A04_2021/)

<a id="t-070"></a><a id="f-070"></a>
#### F-070 · Allocation of Resources without Limits

**Severity:** 🟡 Medium  ·  **Component:** [C-10](#c-10) - Web3 / Wallet / NFT Surface  ·  **Location:** `routes/web3Wallet.ts:16`

**Issue:** contractExploitListener does `walletsConnected.add(req.body.walletAddress)` on every POST /rest/web3/walletExploitAddress, and walletNFTVerify / the NFT listener feed addressesMinted (`routes/nftMint.ts:10`,42). The web3 routes carry no rate-limit middleware (express-rate-limit is applied to other routes at `server.ts:343`,459-472 but not to lines 641-645).

Unbounded memory growth from attacker-supplied addresses plus absent rate limiting enables a low-cost memory-exhaustion DoS of the Node process.

**Evidence:** ◌ ambiguous - Module-level Sets (walletsConnected, addressesMinted) grow per request with no size cap or TTL, and the web3 route block at `server.ts:641-645` has no rate-limit middleware.

**Fix:** Bound the request rate and the per-request resource budget on this endpoint → <span style="color:#888888">❸</span> [M-070](#m-070) — Add rate limiting and bounded/TTL eviction to web3 wallet tracking sets (`web3Wallet.ts:16`)

**Classification:** Denial of Service · [CWE-770](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/770.html) · [OWASP A04:2021](https://owasp.org/Top10/A04_2021/)

_**Severity annotation:** rows tagged `*(raw Critical)*` had a Critical-class impact that was capped to a lower effective severity by the triage stage (likelihood downgrade or `data/severity-caps.yaml` rule). The rendered severity is the **effective** severity used for ranking and prioritisation; the raw severity is preserved here so reviewers can re-evaluate the cap decision._

_**Evidence verification:** rows tagged `⚠ (evidence refuted)` were re-checked by the Phase 10a evidence-verifier (see `.evidence-verification.json`) and the cited `file:line` did **not** show the claimed weakness. Their raw severity is preserved, but chain-elevation has been suppressed by the triage stage. Rows tagged `◌ (evidence ambiguous)` could not be confirmed or refuted from the cited snippet alone - a human reviewer should decide whether to keep, downgrade, or remove these findings._

## 8. Abuse Cases

_Abuse cases describe end-to-end attack scenarios that chain individual findings into an exploitation path. Each case is **mandatory** - defined in the org profile / plugin library and evaluated against every repository. Every chain step references a finding from [§7 Findings Register](#7-findings-register); each step is code-confirmed against the repository and the chain verdict is folded deterministically from the per-step results, never rated by hand._

| # | Scenario | Actor | Combined Risk | Verdict |
|--------|------------------------------------|------------------|-------------|--------------|
| [AC-T-001](#ac-t-001) | Account Takeover via Stored XSS + Token<br/>Hijacking | external-attacker | 🔴 Critical | ⚠ Fully viable |
| [AC-T-002](#ac-t-002) | Bulk Data Exfiltration via Broken Object<br/>Authorization | authenticated-user | 🔴 Critical | ⚠ Fully viable |
| [AC-T-003](#ac-t-003) | Privilege Escalation to Admin via JWT<br/>Algorithm Confusion | external-attacker | 🔴 Critical | ⚠ Fully viable |
| [AC-T-004](#ac-t-004) | Privilege Escalation via Mass-Assignment on<br/>Registration | external-attacker | 🔴 Critical | ⚠ Fully viable |
| [AC-T-005](#ac-t-005) | Authentication Bypass via Exposed Secret<br/>Material | external-attacker | 🔴 Critical | ◐ Partially blocked |
| [AC-T-006](#ac-t-006) | Remote Code Execution via Server-Side<br/>Injection | external-attacker | 🔴 Critical | ◐ Partially blocked |

_Verdict: ⚠ Fully viable - no effective control blocks this chain · ◐ Partially blocked - at least one step has a compensating control but the chain is not fully closed · ✓ Mitigated - chain is broken at a verified step · ? Inconclusive - could not be verified end-to-end._

---

### <a id="ac-t-001"></a>AC-T-001 — Account Takeover via Stored XSS + Token Hijacking

> **Source:** mandatory · **Actor:** external-attacker - unauthenticated external attacker · **Combined Risk:** 🔴 Critical · **Verdict:** ⚠ Fully viable

**Goal:** Obtain persistent authenticated access as an arbitrary user without valid credentials.

**Prerequisite:** Attacker can submit content that is later rendered to other users (`e.g`. feedback, comments, profile fields).

**Attack chain**

| Step | Finding | Outcome |
|--------|------------------------------------------------|----------------------|
| 1 | 🟠 [F-035](#f-035) — Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) (`search-result.component.ts:143`) | Attacker JavaScript executes in the victim's<br/>browser session. |
| 2 | 🟠 [F-046](#f-046) — Insecure Client-Side Storage of JWT in localStorage (`oauth.component.ts:51`) | Token exfiltrated from local/session storage<br/>via the Step 1 payload. |
| 3 | 🟠 [F-019](#f-019) — Untrusted URL-Fragment Parsing of OAuth Token (`oauth.component.ts:71`) | Exfiltrated token accepted for a new<br/>session; absence of token binding / PKCE<br/>removes the last server-side revocation<br/>opportunity. |

**Why combined risk exceeds individual ratings**

Individually the XSS sink and the web-readable token storage rate below Critical, but chained they form a repeatable credential-theft path: a single stored payload causes indefinite session compromise for every user who views the affected page.

**Blocking mitigations**

Implementing any single mitigation below severs the chain at the named step, so the end-to-end abuse can no longer complete:

- <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-035](#m-035) — Remove bypassSecurityTrustHtml on the search term and render it via interpolation (**P2**): remediating 🟠 [F-035](#f-035) — Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) breaks the chain at **Step 1**, removing the link the rest of the chain depends on.
- <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-046](#m-046) — Move the session token out of localStorage into an HttpOnly Secure SameSite cookie via a BFF (**P2**): remediating 🟠 [F-046](#f-046) — Insecure Client-Side Storage of JWT in localStorage breaks the chain at **Step 2**, removing the link the rest of the chain depends on.
- <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-019](#m-019) — Validate OAuth state and token claims; perform the token exchange server-side (**P2**): remediating 🟠 [F-019](#f-019) — Untrusted URL-Fragment Parsing of OAuth Token breaks the chain at **Step 3**, removing the link the rest of the chain depends on.

---

### <a id="ac-t-002"></a>AC-T-002 — Bulk Data Exfiltration via Broken Object Authorization

> **Source:** mandatory · **Actor:** authenticated-user - authenticated low-privilege user · **Combined Risk:** 🔴 Critical · **Verdict:** ⚠ Fully viable

**Goal:** Enumerate and exfiltrate other users' records, then escalate own permissions via unguarded mass assignment.

**Prerequisite:** Attacker holds a valid, non-privileged user account.

**Attack chain**

| Step | Finding | Outcome |
|--------|------------------------------------------------|----------------------|
| 1 | 🟠 [F-005](#f-005) — Sensitive Routes Registered Without Authorization (`server.ts:310`)<br/>`routes/basket.ts:19` | Attacker enumerates and retrieves records<br/>for arbitrary object IDs; no ownership<br/>comparison is performed. |
| 2 | 🔴 [F-002](#f-002) — Systemic Mass Assignment of Privileged Fields (`verify.ts:51`)<br/>`server.ts:484` | Update endpoint persists an unfiltered `role`<br/>(or equivalent) field supplied in the<br/>request body. |

**Why combined risk exceeds individual ratings**

The ownership gap exposes every record, and the mass-assignment gap lets the same low-privilege actor self-elevate - together they turn a single compromised account into full tenant data access and role escalation.

**Blocking mitigations**

Implementing any single mitigation below severs the chain at the named step, so the end-to-end abuse can no longer complete:

- <span style="color:#555555">❷</span> [M-005](#m-005) — Add an explicit auth middleware (`isAuthorized()` / `passport.authenticate()` / requireAuth) to the route registration, or mark the route intentionally public via `app.get`(...) for read-only access only. (**P2**): remediating 🟠 [F-005](#f-005) — Sensitive Routes Registered Without Authorization breaks the chain at **Step 1**, removing the link the rest of the chain depends on.
- <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-002](#m-002) — Implement centralized input validation and output encoding middleware (**P1**): remediating 🔴 [F-002](#f-002) — Systemic Mass Assignment of Privileged Fields breaks the chain at **Step 2**, removing the link the rest of the chain depends on.

---

### <a id="ac-t-003"></a>AC-T-003 — Privilege Escalation to Admin via JWT Algorithm Confusion

> **Source:** mandatory · **Actor:** external-attacker - unauthenticated external attacker · **Combined Risk:** 🔴 Critical · **Verdict:** ⚠ Fully viable

**Goal:** Forge an admin-role JWT without knowledge of the signing secret.

**Prerequisite:** Attacker can obtain any valid JWT issued by the system (`e.g`. by registering a free account).

**Attack chain**

| Step | Finding | Outcome |
|--------|------------------------------------------------|----------------------|
| 1 | 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — Insecure JWT Verification (`insecurity.ts:55`) | Verifier accepts attacker-chosen `alg` (`e.g`.<br/>`none` or HMAC-with-public-key), allowing<br/>token re-signing without the secret. |
| 2 | 🔴 [F-010](#f-010) — Insecure Direct Object Reference (`dataExport.ts:26`)<br/>`lib/insecurity.ts:156` | Forged `role: admin` claim is accepted as<br/>authoritative because the role is not<br/>re-fetched from the database per request. |

**Why combined risk exceeds individual ratings**

Algorithm confusion alone yields a forgeable token; trusting the in-token role claim turns that forgery into instant admin access - neither gap is Critical in isolation, but the chain is a full authentication bypass.

**Blocking mitigations**

Implementing any single mitigation below severs the chain at the named step, so the end-to-end abuse can no longer complete:

- <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-008](#m-008) — Pin JWT verification to RS256 and reject alg:none in `lib/insecurity.ts` (**P1**): remediating 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — Insecure JWT Verification breaks the chain at **Step 1**, removing the link the rest of the chain depends on.
- <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-010](#m-010) — Replace `req.body.UserId`/userId/ownerId with `req.user.id` (or equivalent session-derived identity) in every WHERE/filter clause. (**P1**): remediating 🔴 [F-010](#f-010) — Insecure Direct Object Reference breaks the chain at **Step 2**, removing the link the rest of the chain depends on.

---

### <a id="ac-t-004"></a>AC-T-004 — Privilege Escalation via Mass-Assignment on Registration

> **Source:** mandatory · **Actor:** external-attacker - unauthenticated external attacker · **Combined Risk:** 🔴 Critical · **Verdict:** ⚠ Fully viable

**Goal:** Obtain an administrator account without any existing privilege.

**Prerequisite:** Self-registration is open (one unauthenticated POST).

**Attack chain**

| Step | Finding | Outcome |
|--------|------------------------------------------------|----------------------|
| 1 | 🔴 [F-002](#f-002) — Systemic Mass Assignment of Privileged Fields (`verify.ts:51`)<br/>`server.ts:484` | The account-creation handler persists the<br/>request body wholesale, so a client-supplied<br/>`role` (or `isAdmin`) field is written verbatim. |

**Why combined risk exceeds individual ratings**

A single unauthenticated request mints an admin account when the registration handler trusts a client-supplied role field - the most direct full-compromise path in role-based apps with open sign-up.

**Blocking mitigations**

Implementing any single mitigation below severs the chain at the named step, so the end-to-end abuse can no longer complete:

- <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-002](#m-002) — Implement centralized input validation and output encoding middleware (**P1**): remediating 🔴 [F-002](#f-002) — Systemic Mass Assignment of Privileged Fields breaks the chain at **Step 1**, removing the link the rest of the chain depends on.

---

### <a id="ac-t-005"></a>AC-T-005 — Authentication Bypass via Exposed Secret Material

> **Source:** mandatory · **Actor:** external-attacker - unauthenticated external attacker · **Combined Risk:** 🔴 Critical · **Verdict:** ◐ Partially blocked

**Goal:** Forge trusted tokens / credentials and impersonate any user.

**Prerequisite:** Signing material or other secrets are reachable (committed to a public repo, served by an unauthenticated route, or in an exposed directory).

**Attack chain**

| Step | Finding | Outcome |
|--------|------------------------------------------------|----------------------|
| 1 | 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — Hardcoded Cryptographic Key (`insecurity.ts:21`) | A private key, signing secret, or credential<br/>file is committed to the source repository<br/>or served without authentication. |
| 2 | 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — Hardcoded Cryptographic Key (`insecurity.ts:21`) | The exposed key/secret is the same one the<br/>server trusts, so a token signed with it (or<br/>the leaked credential) is accepted as<br/>authentic. |

**Why combined risk exceeds individual ratings**

Exposed signing material collapses the entire authentication boundary: any attacker who reads the key can mint a valid token for any identity or role, with no credential ever required.

**Blocking mitigations**

Implementing any single mitigation below severs the chain at the named step, so the end-to-end abuse can no longer complete:

- <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-007](#m-007) — Load the JWT signing key from a secret manager and rotate the leaked key (**P1**): remediating 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — Hardcoded Cryptographic Key breaks the chain at **Step 1**, removing the link the rest of the chain depends on.

---

### <a id="ac-t-006"></a>AC-T-006 — Remote Code Execution via Server-Side Injection

> **Source:** mandatory · **Actor:** external-attacker - unauthenticated external attacker · **Combined Risk:** 🔴 Critical · **Verdict:** ◐ Partially blocked

**Goal:** Execute arbitrary code in the application process.

**Prerequisite:** An input reaches a server-side interpreter / template / eval.

**Attack chain**

| Step | Finding | Outcome |
|--------|------------------------------------------------|----------------------|
| 1 | 🔴 [F-013](#f-013) — Server-Side Code Evaluation of Untrusted Input (`b2bOrder.ts:23`) | Attacker-controlled input is passed to `eval`,<br/>a server-side template engine, an unsafe<br/>sandbox, or an unsafe deserializer. |

**Why combined risk exceeds individual ratings**

A single injection into a server-side interpreter yields code execution in the application process - the highest-impact outcome, granting full filesystem and network access from one unauthenticated request.

**Blocking mitigations**

Implementing any single mitigation below severs the chain at the named step, so the end-to-end abuse can no longer complete:

- <span style="color:#111111">❶</span> [M-013](#m-013) — Replace safeEval/vm evaluation of orderLinesData with a declarative JSON parser and schema validation (**P1**): remediating 🔴 [F-013](#f-013) — Server-Side Code Evaluation of Untrusted Input breaks the chain at **Step 1**, removing the link the rest of the chain depends on.

---

### P1 — Immediate

<a id="m-002"></a>
#### M-002 — Implement centralized input validation and output encoding middleware

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-002](#f-002) — Systemic Mass Assignment of Privileged Fields (`verify.ts:51`)

**Priority:** P1 - Immediate · **Effort:** Low · **File:** `server.ts:408`

**How:** In the `POST /api/Users` pre-handler (`server.ts:408`), delete `req.body.role` (and `req.body`.`deluxeToken`) before the finale resource processes it. Set role server-side to 'customer' on the created model regardless of input; promote to admin only through an authenticated admin-only endpoint. Add an integration test asserting that `POST /api/Users` with role:'admin' yields a customer account.

1. In the `POST /api/Users` pre-handler (`server.ts:408`), delete `req.body.role` (and `req.body`.`deluxeToken`) before the finale resource processes it.
2. Set role server-side to 'customer' on the created model regardless of input; promote to admin only through an authenticated admin-only endpoint.
3. Add an integration test asserting that `POST /api/Users` with role:'admin' yields a customer account.

```javascript
app.post('/api/Users', (req, _res, next) => {
  delete req.body.role; delete req.body.deluxeToken
  next()
})
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Mass_Assignment_Cheat_Sheet.html

---

<a id="m-007"></a>
#### M-007 — Load the JWT signing key from a secret manager and rotate the leaked key

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-007](#f-007) — Hardcoded Cryptographic Key (`insecurity.ts:21`)

**Priority:** P1 - Immediate · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `lib/insecurity.ts:21`

**How:** Remove the inline PEM at `lib/insecurity.ts:21` and read the private key from an environment variable or secret manager (AWS KMS, HashiCorp Vault) at startup; never commit key material. Generate a fresh RSA keypair, replace encryptionkeys/jwt.pub, and invalidate all tokens signed with the old key (purge `git history of the leaked key with git filter-repo)`. Add a CI secret-scanning gate (gitleaks/trufflehog) to block future committed keys.

1. Remove the inline PEM at `lib/insecurity.ts:21` and read the private key from an environment variable or secret manager (AWS KMS, HashiCorp Vault) at startup; never commit key material.
2. Generate a fresh RSA keypair, replace encryptionkeys/jwt.pub, and invalidate all tokens signed with the old key (purge `git history of the leaked key with git filter-repo)`.
3. Add a CI secret-scanning gate (gitleaks/trufflehog) to block future committed keys.

```javascript
const privateKey = fs.readFileSync(process.env.JWT_PRIVATE_KEY_PATH, 'utf8')
export const authorize = (user = {}) => jwt.sign(user, privateKey, { expiresIn: '6h', algorithm: 'RS256' })
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Secrets_Management_Cheat_Sheet.html

---

<a id="m-008"></a>
#### M-008 — Pin JWT verification to RS256 and reject alg:none in lib/insecurity.ts

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-008](#f-008) — Insecure JWT Verification (`insecurity.ts:55`)

**Priority:** P1 - Immediate · **Effort:** Low · **File:** `lib/insecurity.ts:55`

**How:** Replace the raw `jws.verify` call with `jwt.verify(token, publicKey, { algorithms: ['RS256'] })` so the algorithm is server-controlled, not header-controlled. Explicitly reject tokens whose header alg is 'none' or any HMAC variant before decoding. Audit all callers of `decode()` (`isAccounting`, `isDeluxe`, `isCustomer`, `routes/currentUser.ts`, `routes/2fa.ts`) to ensure they verify before trusting claims.

1. Replace the raw `jws.verify` call with `jwt.verify(token, publicKey, { algorithms: ['RS256'] })` so the algorithm is server-controlled, not header-controlled.
2. Explicitly reject tokens whose header alg is 'none' or any HMAC variant before decoding.
3. Audit all callers of `decode()` (`isAccounting`, `isDeluxe`, `isCustomer`, `routes/currentUser.ts`, `routes/2fa.ts`) to ensure they verify before trusting claims.

```javascript
export const verify = (token: string) => {
  if (!token) return false
  try { jwt.verify(token, publicKey, { algorithms: ['RS256'] }); return true }
  catch { return false }
}
```

**Reference:** CWE-347

---

<a id="m-009"></a>
#### M-009 — Stop deriving passwords from the email claim; provision OAuth accounts without a guessable password

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-009](#f-009) — Derived Password from OAuth Email Claim (`oauth.component.ts:30`)

**Priority:** P1 - Immediate · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:30`

**How:** Do not set or compute a user-facing password during OAuth provisioning. Mark OAuth accounts as federated and disable password login for them on the backend. If a credential placeholder is unavoidable, generate it server-side with a CSPRNG (`e.g`. 32 random bytes) and never echo it to the client or derive it from any claim. Bind the local session strictly to a verified OAuth token exchange performed server-side, so possession of the email alone never yields authentication.

1. Do not set or compute a user-facing password during OAuth provisioning. Mark OAuth accounts as federated and disable password login for them on the backend.
2. If a credential placeholder is unavoidable, generate it server-side with a CSPRNG (`e.g`. 32 random bytes) and never echo it to the client or derive it from any claim.
3. Bind the local session strictly to a verified OAuth token exchange performed server-side, so possession of the email alone never yields authentication.

```javascript
// remove the derivation entirely
// BAD: const password = btoa(profile.email.split('').reverse().join(''))
// GOOD: backend creates a federated account, no password login allowed
this.userService.oauthLogin(token).subscribe(/* session set by server, httpOnly cookie */)
```

**Reference:** CWE-287

---

<a id="m-010"></a>
#### M-010 — Replace req.body.UserId/userId/ownerId with req.user.id (or equivalent session-derived identity) in every WHERE/filter clause.

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-010](#f-010) — Insecure Direct Object Reference (`dataExport.ts:26`)

**Priority:** P1 - Immediate · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `routes/dataExport.ts:26`

```typescript
// Ownership check before touching a resource.
const basket = await Basket.findByPk(req.params.id)
if (!basket || basket.UserId !== req.user.id) return res.status(403).end()
```

**Verification:** Authenticate as user A; request `/api/Baskets/<B's id>` and confirm 403.

<a id="m-011"></a>
#### M-011 — Replace MD5 password hashing with per-user salted bcrypt/argon2 in the User model setter

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-011](#f-011) — Unsalted MD5 password storage (`user.ts:76`)

**Priority:** P1 - Immediate · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `models/user.ts:76`

**How:** Replace `security.hash()` in the password setter (`models/user.ts:76`) with an adaptive password hash: bcrypt (cost >= 12) via the existing bcryptjs dependency, or argon2id. Store the full algorithm-tagged hash string (`e.g`. $2b$12$...) so salt and cost travel with the value; drop the MD5 path in `lib/insecurity.ts:41` for credential use. Add a transparent rehash-on-login migration: on successful authentication, if the stored hash is legacy MD5, recompute with bcrypt and update the row. Verify the login comparison path uses a constant-time verify (`bcrypt.compare`) rather than re-hashing and string-equality.

1. Replace `security.hash()` in the password setter (`models/user.ts:76`) with an adaptive password hash: bcrypt (cost >= 12) via the existing bcryptjs dependency, or argon2id.
2. Store the full algorithm-tagged hash string (`e.g`. $2b$12$...) so salt and cost travel with the value; drop the MD5 path in `lib/insecurity.ts:41` for credential use.
3. Add a transparent rehash-on-login migration: on successful authentication, if the stored hash is legacy MD5, recompute with bcrypt and update the row.
4. Verify the login comparison path uses a constant-time verify (`bcrypt.compare`) rather than re-hashing and string-equality.

```javascript
import bcrypt from 'bcryptjs'
// User model password setter
password: {
  type: DataTypes.STRING,
  set (clearTextPassword: string) {
    this.setDataValue('password', bcrypt.hashSync(clearTextPassword, 12))
  }
}
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Password_Storage_Cheat_Sheet.html

---

<a id="m-012"></a>
#### M-012 — Disable DTD loading and external-entity resolution in parseXmlString

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-012](#f-012) — XML External Entity Injection (`xml.ts:35`)

**Priority:** P1 - Immediate · **Effort:** Low · **File:** `lib/xml.ts:35`

**How:** Remove `XML_PARSE_NOENT` and `XML_PARSE_DTDLOAD` from the ParseOption bitmask at `lib/xml.ts:35` - parse with entity substitution and DTD loading off so SYSTEM/file:// entities never resolve. Delete the `xmlRegisterFsInputProviders()` call at `lib/xml.ts:21` so the WASM parser has no host filesystem access. Stop reflecting the parsed XML back to the caller: replace `utils.trunc(xmlString, 400)` in the `routes/fileUpload.ts:79` error with a static message so even residual entity content is not disclosed. Add `security.isAuthorized()` in front of `POST /file-upload` at `server.ts:309` to remove the anonymous attack path.

1. Remove `XML_PARSE_NOENT` and `XML_PARSE_DTDLOAD` from the ParseOption bitmask at `lib/xml.ts:35` - parse with entity substitution and DTD loading off so SYSTEM/file:// entities never resolve.

1. Implement server-side authorization middleware on every privileged `/api/*` and `/rest/*` route that verifies the JWT signature and checks the role claim - never rely on the Angular guard.
2. Keep the client guards for UX but document that they are not a trust boundary; verify the JWT signature server-side before honoring any role.
3. Add automated tests that call privileged endpoints directly (no UI) with non-admin and forged tokens and assert 401/403.

```javascript
// backend guard, not the SPA
function requireRole(role) {
  return (req, res, next) => {
    const p = jwt.verify(req.token, PUBLIC_KEY) // signature verified
    if (p?.data?.role !== role) return res.sendStatus(403)
    next()
  }
}
```

<a id="m-020"></a>
#### M-020 — Replace OAuth implicit flow with authorization-code + PKCE and validate state/nonce server-side

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-020](#f-020) — OAuth Implicit Flow / Token in URL Fragment (`app.routing.ts:257`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** High · **File:** `frontend/src/app/app.routing.ts:257`

**How:** Migrate to OAuth 2.0 Authorization Code flow with PKCE (RFC 7636): request `response_type=code` and a `code_challenge` (S256), never `response_type=token`. Generate a cryptographically random `state` before redirect, persist it in `sessionStorage`, and reject the callback in `oauthMatcher`/OAuthComponent if the returned `state` does not match. Exchange the authorization code for tokens on the Express backend so the access/refresh tokens never enter the browser URL or JavaScript scope; return only a short-lived session via an HttpOnly Secure SameSite=Strict cookie. Stop sourcing route data from `window.location.href`; once code flow is in place the fragment-parsing matcher can be deleted.

1. Migrate to OAuth 2.0 Authorization Code flow with PKCE (RFC 7636): request `response_type=code` and a `code_challenge` (S256), never `response_type=token`.
2. Generate a cryptographically random `state` before redirect, persist it in `sessionStorage`, and reject the callback in `oauthMatcher`/OAuthComponent if the returned `state` does not match.
3. Exchange the authorization code for tokens on the Express backend so the access/refresh tokens never enter the browser URL or JavaScript scope; return only a short-lived session via an HttpOnly Secure SameSite=Strict cookie.
4. Stop sourcing route data from `window.location.href`; once code flow is in place the fragment-parsing matcher can be deleted.

```javascript
// authorization-code + PKCE (conceptual)
const verifier = base64url(crypto.getRandomValues(new Uint8Array(32)))
const challenge = base64url(await sha256(verifier))
const state = base64url(crypto.getRandomValues(new Uint8Array(16)))
sessionStorage.setItem('oauth_state', state)
location.href = `${authz}?response_type=code&code_challenge=${challenge}&code_challenge_method=S256&state=${state}&...`
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/OAuth2_Cheat_Sheet.html

<a id="m-021"></a>
#### M-021 — Require signed nonce proving wallet control before honoring walletNFTVerify

- 🔴 [F-021](#f-021) — Wallet Ownership Spoofing on NFT verify (`nftMint.ts:41`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `routes/nftMint.ts:41`

**How:** Issue a server-generated, single-use nonce bound to the user session; require the client to sign it with the wallet (personal_sign) and submit the signature alongside `walletAddress`. Recover the signer with ethers `verifyMessage(nonce, signature)` and assert the recovered address === `req.body`.`walletAddress` before consulting `addressesMinted`. Expire and invalidate the nonce on first use to prevent replay; bind the solved challenge to the authenticated user, not just the address string.

1. Issue a server-generated, single-use nonce bound to the user session; require the client to sign it with the wallet (personal_sign) and submit the signature alongside `walletAddress`.
2. Recover the signer with ethers `verifyMessage(nonce, signature)` and assert the recovered address === `req.body`.`walletAddress` before consulting `addressesMinted`.
3. Expire and invalidate the nonce on first use to prevent replay; bind the solved challenge to the authenticated user, not just the address string.

```javascript
const { verifyMessage } = await import('ethers')
const signer = verifyMessage(req.session.web3Nonce, req.body.signature)
if (signer.toLowerCase() !== req.body.walletAddress.toLowerCase()) {
  return res.status(401).json({ success: false })
}
// nonce single-use
delete req.session.web3Nonce
```

**Reference:** CWE-290

#### M-022 — Replace substring redirect allowlist with parsed-origin exact match in isRedirectAllowed

```javascript
export const isRedirectAllowed = (url: string) => {
  let target: URL
  try { target = new URL(url) } catch { return false }
  return [...redirectAllowlist].some(a => {
    const allowed = new URL(a)
    return target.origin === allowed.origin && target.pathname === allowed.pathname
  })
}
```

<a id="m-023"></a>
#### M-023 — Add a Socket\.IO handshake authentication middleware that validates the session JWT before accepting connections

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-023](#f-023) — Unauthenticated WebSocket Channel (`registerWebsocketEvents.ts:23`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:23`

**How:** Register an `io.use((socket, next) => {...})` middleware in `registerWebsocketEvents.ts` before the `io.on('connection')` block. Read the JWT from `socket.handshake.auth.token` (set by the client) and verify it with the same `insecurity.verify()` used by the REST tier. Reject the handshake with `next(new Error('unauthorized'))` when the token is absent or invalid, and attach the decoded principal to `socket.data.user` for downstream per-event authorization. Update frontend `Services/socket-io.service.ts` to pass the bearer token via the `auth` option: `io(origin, { path, auth: { token } })`. Gate the per-connection notification replay (lines 29-31) and every `socket.on(...)` handler behind `socket.data.user` so unauthenticated sockets receive and trigger nothing.

1. Register an `io.use((socket, next) => {...})` middleware in `registerWebsocketEvents.ts` before the `io.on('connection')` block. Read the JWT from `socket.handshake.auth.token` (set by the client) and verify it with the same `insecurity.verify()` used by the REST tier.
2. Reject the handshake with `next(new Error('unauthorized'))` when the token is absent or invalid, and attach the decoded principal to `socket.data.user` for downstream per-event authorization.
3. Update frontend `Services/socket-io.service.ts` to pass the bearer token via the `auth` option: `io(origin, { path, auth: { token } })`.
4. Gate the per-connection notification replay (lines 29-31) and every `socket.on(...)` handler behind `socket.data.user` so unauthenticated sockets receive and trigger nothing.

```javascript
io.use((socket, next) => {
  const token = socket.handshake.auth?.token
  const user = token && security.verify(token)
  if (!user) return next(new Error('unauthorized'))
  socket.data.user = user
  next()
})
io.on('connection', (socket) => { /* socket.data.user is now trusted */ })
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/HTML5_Security_Cheat_Sheet.html#websockets

<a id="m-024"></a>
#### M-024 — Eliminate the evaluation path and parse orderLinesData with a prototype-safe JSON parser

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-024](#f-024) — Prototype Pollution via Sandbox Escape (`b2bOrder.ts:23`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `routes/b2bOrder.ts:23`

**How:** Remove the notevil/vm evaluation (see 🔴 [F-013](#f-013)); polluting writes are only reachable because the string is interpreted. When parsing the now-data-only `orderLinesData`, strip dangerous keys before use: reject any object containing __proto__, constructor, or prototype keys. Create order-line objects with `Object.create(null)` or guard reads so a polluted prototype cannot influence business logic.

1. Remove the notevil/vm evaluation (see 🔴 [F-013](#f-013)); polluting writes are only reachable because the string is interpreted.
2. When parsing the now-data-only `orderLinesData`, strip dangerous keys before use: reject any object containing __proto__, constructor, or prototype keys.
3. Create order-line objects with `Object.create(null)` or guard reads so a polluted prototype cannot influence business logic.

```javascript
const FORBIDDEN = new Set(['__proto__', 'constructor', 'prototype'])
function assertClean (obj) {
  for (const k of Object.keys(obj)) {
    if (FORBIDDEN.has(k)) throw new Error('forbidden key')
    if (obj[k] && typeof obj[k] === 'object') assertClean(obj[k])
  }
}
assertClean(JSON.parse(body.orderLinesData))
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Prototype_Pollution_Prevention_Cheat_Sheet.html

<a id="m-025"></a>
#### M-025 — Add a strict Content-Security-Policy and server-side output encoding

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-025](#f-025) — Persistent XSS surface left open by disabled XSS protections (`server.ts:188`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `server.ts:188`

**How:** Configure `helmet.contentSecurityPolicy()` with a restrictive default-src 'self' policy and no unsafe-inline for scripts. Sanitize/encode user-supplied fields server-side before persistence using the existing sanitize-html, and encode on output in the SPA. Store the session token in an HttpOnly Secure cookie rather than `localStorage` to remove it from XSS reach.

1. Configure `helmet.contentSecurityPolicy()` with a restrictive default-src 'self' policy and no unsafe-inline for scripts.
2. Sanitize/encode user-supplied fields server-side before persistence using the existing sanitize-html, and encode on output in the SPA.
3. Store the session token in an HttpOnly Secure cookie rather than `localStorage` to remove it from XSS reach.

```javascript
app.use(helmet.contentSecurityPolicy({ directives: { defaultSrc: ["'self'"], scriptSrc: ["'self'"], objectSrc: ["'none'"] } }))
```

#### M-026 — Enforce coupon policy in code, not prompt, and constrain tool inputs

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-026](#f-026) — Indirect prompt injection in chatbot grants unauthorized coupons (`chat.ts:205`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `routes/chat.ts:205`

**How:** Clamp and authorize the discount server-side inside `generateCoupon`.execute: verify the caller's authenticated identity and a real damaged-order record, and hard-cap discount at 10 regardless of the model's argument. Do not place secret business rules (the 15% escalation discount) in the system prompt; gate them behind server logic. Add input/output guards on the chat messages (length caps, instruction-injection screening) before invoking the model.

1. Clamp and authorize the discount server-side inside `generateCoupon`.execute: verify the caller's authenticated identity and a real damaged-order record, and hard-cap discount at 10 regardless of the model's argument.
2. Do not place secret business rules (the 15% escalation discount) in the system prompt; gate them behind server logic.
3. Add input/output guards on the chat messages (length caps, instruction-injection screening) before invoking the model.

```javascript
execute: async ({ discount }) => {
  const uid = await getUserId(req); if (!uid) return { error: 'unauthenticated' }
  if (!(await hasVerifiedDamagedOrder(uid))) return { error: 'not eligible' }
  const safe = Math.min(Math.max(discount, 0), 10)
  return { couponCode: security.generateCoupon(safe), discount: safe }
}
```

<a id="m-029"></a>
#### M-029 — Enforce coupon discount ceiling in tool code, not in the system prompt

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-029](#f-029) — Prompt Injection (`chat.ts:191`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `routes/chat.ts:191`

**How:** Move every business rule out of the system prompt into the `generateCoupon` `execute()` body: clamp `discount` to the server constant (`e.g`. `Math.min(discount, 10)`), and verify the damaged-order + rejected-return preconditions against the database before calling `security.generateCoupon`. Treat the entire `messages` array as untrusted: reject or strip any element whose `role` is `system` or `assistant` so callers cannot fabricate authoritative turns; keep only `role: 'user'` content. Add a deterministic guard so the tool refuses when preconditions are unmet regardless of what the model decided, and log the refusal.

1. Move every business rule out of the system prompt into the `generateCoupon` `execute()` body: clamp `discount` to the server constant (`e.g`. `Math.min(discount, 10)`), and verify the damaged-order + rejected-return preconditions against the database before calling `security.generateCoupon`.
2. Treat the entire `messages` array as untrusted: reject or strip any element whose `role` is `system` or `assistant` so callers cannot fabricate authoritative turns; keep only `role: 'user'` content.
3. Add a deterministic guard so the tool refuses when preconditions are unmet regardless of what the model decided, and log the refusal.

```javascript
execute: async ({ discount }) => {
  const capped = Math.min(Math.max(discount, 0), MAX_DISCOUNT) // MAX_DISCOUNT = 10
  const order = await verifyDamagedOrder(await getUserId(req))
  if (!order?.rejectedReturn) return { error: 'Coupon conditions not met' }
  return { couponCode: security.generateCoupon(capped), discount: capped }
}
```

**Reference:** https://genai.owasp.org/llmrisk/llm01-prompt-injection/

```javascript
for (const field of requestedFields) {
  if (ALLOWED.has(field) && user?.data[field] !== undefined) baseUser[field] = user.data[field]
}
```

<a id="m-044"></a>
#### M-044 — Encrypt or tokenize stored card numbers with an application-level AEAD setter on the Card model

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-044](#f-044) — Payment card number stored in cleartext (`card.ts:38`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `models/card.ts:38`

**How:** Stop storing the raw PAN: tokenize via the payment processor and persist only the token plus last-four, or apply application-level AES-256-GCM encryption in a Card model setter before `setDataValue`. Move the encryption key out of source into a secrets manager / env var; never co-locate it with the SQLite file. Change the column type to a STRING/BLOB capable of holding ciphertext+IV+tag rather than INTEGER. If retaining encrypted PANs, scope access and add field-level decrypt only at the payment route, keeping `cardNum` opaque elsewhere.

1. Stop storing the raw PAN: tokenize via the payment processor and persist only the token plus last-four, or apply application-level AES-256-GCM encryption in a Card model setter before `setDataValue`.
2. Move the encryption key out of source into a secrets manager / env var; never co-locate it with the SQLite file.
3. Change the column type to a STRING/BLOB capable of holding ciphertext+IV+tag rather than INTEGER.
4. If retaining encrypted PANs, scope access and add field-level decrypt only at the payment route, keeping `cardNum` opaque elsewhere.

```javascript
cardNum: {
  type: DataTypes.STRING,
  set (pan: string) {
    const iv = crypto.randomBytes(12)
    const c = crypto.createCipheriv('aes-256-gcm', KEY, iv)
    const ct = Buffer.concat([c.update(String(pan), 'utf8'), c.final()])
    this.setDataValue('cardNum', Buffer.concat([iv, c.getAuthTag(), ct]).toString('base64'))
  }
}
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Cryptographic_Storage_Cheat_Sheet.html
