<a id="m-045"></a>
#### M-045 — Validate imageUrl against an allowlist and block internal/link-local targets before fetch

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-045](#f-045) — Server-Side Request Forgery (`profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`

**How:** Before `fetch()` at `profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`, parse the URL with new `URL()` and reject any scheme other than https, then resolve the hostname and reject RFC1918, loopback, link-local (169.254.0.0/16), and IPv6 ULA/loopback addresses. Re-validate the resolved IP at connection time (or use an SSRF-hardened agent) to defeat DNS rebinding between the check and the fetch. Remove the fallback at line 36 that stores the raw attacker-supplied URL as `profileImage` on fetch failure; on error keep the previous image instead. Cap the streamed response size and set a fetch timeout to bound resource use.

1. Before `fetch()` at `profileImageUrlUpload.ts:24`, parse the URL with new `URL()` and reject any scheme other than https, then resolve the hostname and reject RFC1918, loopback, link-local (169.254.0.0/16), and IPv6 ULA/loopback addresses.
2. Re-validate the resolved IP at connection time (or use an SSRF-hardened agent) to defeat DNS rebinding between the check and the fetch.
3. Remove the fallback at line 36 that stores the raw attacker-supplied URL as `profileImage` on fetch failure; on error keep the previous image instead.
4. Cap the streamed response size and set a fetch timeout to bound resource use.

```javascript
const u = new URL(url)
if (u.protocol !== 'https:') throw new Error('scheme not allowed')
const { address } = await dns.promises.lookup(u.hostname)
if (ipaddr.parse(address).range() !== 'unicast') throw new Error('blocked target')
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Server_Side_Request_Forgery_Prevention_Cheat_Sheet.html

<a id="m-046"></a>
#### M-046 — Move the session token out of localStorage into an HttpOnly Secure SameSite cookie via a BFF

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-046](#f-046) — Insecure Client-Side Storage of JWT in localStorage (`oauth.component.ts:51`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** High · **File:** `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:51`

**How:** Stop calling `localStorage.setItem('token', ...)`; hold the session server-side and issue an HttpOnly Secure SameSite=Strict cookie the SPA cannot read. Have the guards rely on a lightweight `/whoami`/session endpoint rather than decoding a client-readable JWT. Add a Content-Security-Policy (script-src 'self' plus the explicit font origins) to blunt token exfiltration if an XSS slips through.

1. Stop calling `localStorage.setItem('token', ...)`; hold the session server-side and issue an HttpOnly Secure SameSite=Strict cookie the SPA cannot read.
2. Have the guards rely on a lightweight `/whoami`/session endpoint rather than decoding a client-readable JWT.
3. Add a Content-Security-Policy (script-src 'self' plus the explicit font origins) to blunt token exfiltration if an XSS slips through.

```typescript
// Move the JWT out of localStorage into an httpOnly cookie.
res.cookie('session', token, {
  httpOnly: true, secure: true, sameSite: 'lax', maxAge: 3600_000
})
```

**Verification:** Open browser DevTools, run `localStorage.getItem('token')` and confirm `null`.

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/HTML5_Security_Cheat_Sheet.html#local-storage

<a id="m-047"></a>
#### M-047 — Set the session cookie server-side with HttpOnly, Secure and SameSite=Strict

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-047](#f-047) — Session Token Stored in Non-HttpOnly Cookie (`oauth.component.ts:50`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `frontend/src/app/oauth/oauth.component.ts:50`

**How:** Remove the client-side `cookieService.put('token', ...)` call; the Express backend must own session-cookie issuance. Issue the cookie server-side with `HttpOnly; Secure; SameSite=Strict` so JavaScript cannot read it and it is never sent over plaintext. Eliminate the duplicate `localStorage` copy (see 🔴 [F-046](#f-046)) so a single hardened cookie is the only session carrier.

1. Remove the client-side `cookieService.put('token', ...)` call; the Express backend must own session-cookie issuance.
2. Issue the cookie server-side with `HttpOnly; Secure; SameSite=Strict` so JavaScript cannot read it and it is never sent over plaintext.
3. Eliminate the duplicate `localStorage` copy (see 🔴 [F-046](#f-046)) so a single hardened cookie is the only session carrier.

```javascript
// server-side (Express)
res.cookie('token', jwt, { httpOnly: true, secure: true, sameSite: 'strict' })
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Session_Management_Cheat_Sheet.html#cookies

<a id="m-049"></a>
#### M-049 — Key rate limiters on the validated proxy-derived client IP

<a id="m-050"></a>
#### M-050 — Verify tokens with a pinned algorithm and resolve roles from the trusted user record

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-050](#f-050) — Authorization Decisions on Unverified Decoded Claims (`insecurity.ts:156`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `lib/insecurity.ts:156`

**How:** Fix `verify()` to pin RS256 and reject alg:none (🔴 [F-008](#f-008)) so decoded claims are trustworthy. Resolve the caller's role by re-reading the user record from the database by id, rather than trusting the role claim embedded in the token. Apply server-side authorization middleware to every privileged route and add tests asserting forged-role tokens are rejected.

1. Fix `verify()` to pin RS256 and reject alg:none (🔴 [F-008](#f-008)) so decoded claims are trustworthy.
2. Resolve the caller's role by re-reading the user record from the database by id, rather than trusting the role claim embedded in the token.
3. Apply server-side authorization middleware to every privileged route and add tests asserting forged-role tokens are rejected.

```javascript
export const isAccounting = () => async (req, res, next) => {
  const decoded = verify(jwtFrom(req)) && decode(jwtFrom(req))
  const user = decoded && await UserModel.findByPk(decoded.data?.id)
  if (user?.role === roles.accounting) return next()
  res.status(403).json({ error: 'Forbidden' })
}
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Authorization_Cheat_Sheet.html

#### M-051 — Gate sensitive LLM tools behind server-side authorization and least-privilege scope

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-051](#f-051) — Excessive Agency in LLM Tool Invocation (`chat.ts:176`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `routes/chat.ts:176`

**How:** Classify tools by side-effect: keep read-only tools (`searchProducts`, `getProductReviews`) model-invocable; require an explicit server-side eligibility check inside `generateCoupon` that does not consult the prompt. Require an authenticated user for any tool with financial or data-write impact (call `getUserId(req)` and reject when undefined, as `getOrderById` already does at line 159-160). Cap the blast radius: enforce a hard server constant on coupon value and rate-limit coupon issuance per user so even a successful manipulation is bounded.

1. Classify tools by side-effect: keep read-only tools (`searchProducts`, `getProductReviews`) model-invocable; require an explicit server-side eligibility check inside `generateCoupon` that does not consult the prompt.
2. Require an authenticated user for any tool with financial or data-write impact (call `getUserId(req)` and reject when undefined, as `getOrderById` already does at line 159-160).
3. Cap the blast radius: enforce a hard server constant on coupon value and rate-limit coupon issuance per user so even a successful manipulation is bounded.

**Reference:** https://genai.owasp.org/llmrisk/llm062025-excessive-agency/

<a id="m-052"></a>
#### M-052 — Add least-privilege permissions blocks to all 14 unscoped workflows (default contents: read)

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-052](#f-052) — Workflows Missing permissions Block Grant Over-broad `GITHUB_TOKEN` (`ci.yml:1`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `.github/workflows/ci.yml:1`

**How:** Set the organization/repository default workflow permission to read-only (Settings > Actions > Workflow permissions), then add an explicit top-level `permissions:` block to every workflow. Default each workflow to `permissions: { contents: read }` and elevate only the specific scopes a job needs (`e.g`. `packages: write` for the docker push jobs, `contents: write` only for the auto-commit/update workflows). Add a CI policy check (`e.g`. `zizmor` or `actionlint` with a custom rule) that fails when a workflow omits a top-level permissions block.

1. Set the organization/repository default workflow permission to read-only (Settings > Actions > Workflow permissions), then add an explicit top-level `permissions:` block to every workflow.
2. Default each workflow to `permissions: { contents: read }` and elevate only the specific scopes a job needs (`e.g`. `packages: write` for the docker push jobs, `contents: write` only for the auto-commit/update workflows).
3. Add a CI policy check (`e.g`. `zizmor` or `actionlint` with a custom rule) that fails when a workflow omits a top-level permissions block.

```javascript
name: "CI/CD Pipeline"
on: [push, pull_request]
permissions:
  contents: read
jobs:
  docker:
    permissions:
      contents: read
      packages: write
```

<a id="m-053"></a>
#### M-053 — Introduce least-privilege and isolation for the datastore to limit blast radius of injection

**Addresses:**

- 🟠 [F-053](#f-053) — In-process SQLite datastore gives injection full blast radius (`index.ts:41`)

**Priority:** P2 - This Sprint · **Effort:** High · **File:** `models/index.ts:41`

**How:** Eliminate the raw template-string query paths so the ORM's parameterization is the only path to the store, removing the primary injection entry. Move sensitive tables (Users, Cards) toward field-level encryption so an unconstrained read does not yield cleartext secrets even with full DB access. If migrating to a networked DBMS, provision a least-privilege application DB user scoped to required tables/operations rather than a superuser connection. Restrict filesystem permissions on data/juiceshop.sqlite and keep it out of any web-served directory so the file cannot be downloaded directly.

1. Eliminate the raw template-string query paths so the ORM's parameterization is the only path to the store, removing the primary injection entry.
2. Move sensitive tables (Users, Cards) toward field-level encryption so an unconstrained read does not yield cleartext secrets even with full DB access.
3. If migrating to a networked DBMS, provision a least-privilege application DB user scoped to required tables/operations rather than a superuser connection.
4. Restrict filesystem permissions on data/juiceshop.sqlite and keep it out of any web-served directory so the file cannot be downloaded directly.

```typescript
// Centralize access decisions in a single middleware.
function requireRole(role: 'admin' | 'user') {
  return (req, res, next) =>
    req.user?.role === role ? next() : res.status(403).end()
}
```

**Verification:** Cross-check every `/api/*` route for an explicit `requireRole(...)` call; gaps fail CI.

**Reference:** CWE-284

#### M-054 — Add a server-side token revocation list keyed on jti

**How:** Include a unique jti claim in `authorize()` and persist issued/active jtis (or a denylist of revoked ones) in a shared store such as Redis. On logout and on password change, add the affected `jti(s)` to the denylist and check it in `verify()`. Add a per-user `tokenVersion` claim and bump it on password change so all prior tokens fail validation.

2. On logout and on password change, add the affected `jti(s)` to the denylist and check it in `verify()`.
3. Add a per-user `tokenVersion` claim and bump it on password change so all prior tokens fail validation.

```javascript
export const authorize = (user = {}) =>
  jwt.sign({ ...user, jti: crypto.randomUUID() }, privateKey, { expiresIn: '6h', algorithm: 'RS256' })
// verify(): reject if redis.sismember('revoked', decoded.jti)
```

<a id="m-056"></a>
#### M-056 — Configure the production CORS origin allowlist and validate handshake origin server-side

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-056](#f-056) — Missing Socket\.IO Origin Validation (`registerWebsocketEvents.ts:20`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Low · **File:** `lib/startup/registerWebsocketEvents.ts:20`

**How:** Drive the CORS origin from configuration (`config.get`) rather than the hardcoded dev value so production origins are allowlisted explicitly. In the `io.use` handshake middleware, additionally check `socket.handshake.headers.origin` against the allowlist and reject mismatches, so the control is enforced for WebSocket transport and not only CORS-aware browsers. Treat origin validation as defence-in-depth on top of the JWT handshake auth from finding -001, not a substitute for it.

1. Drive the CORS origin from configuration (`config.get`) rather than the hardcoded dev value so production origins are allowlisted explicitly.
2. In the `io.use` handshake middleware, additionally check `socket.handshake.headers.origin` against the allowlist and reject mismatches, so the control is enforced for WebSocket transport and not only CORS-aware browsers.
3. Treat origin validation as defence-in-depth on top of the JWT handshake auth from finding -001, not a substitute for it.

```javascript
const allowed = config.get('server.allowedOrigins')
const io = new Server(server, { cors: { origin: allowed } })
io.use((socket, next) => {
  const o = socket.handshake.headers.origin
  return allowed.includes(o) ? next() : next(new Error('bad origin'))
})
```

**Reference:** CWE-346

#### M-057 — Derive entitlement tokens from a secret-managed key distinct from the JWT key

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-057](#f-057) — Hardcoded HMAC Key Enables Deluxe-Token Forgery (`insecurity.ts:150`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `insecurity.ts:42`

**How:** Move the HMAC key for `deluxeToken` and the answer-hash key (`insecurity.ts:42`) to environment-provided secrets, separate from the JWT signing key. Bind entitlement to a server-side flag on the user record rather than a client-presentable derived token. Rotate both keys after removing them from the repository and `git history`.

1. Move the HMAC key for `deluxeToken` and the answer-hash key (`insecurity.ts:42`) to environment-provided secrets, separate from the JWT signing key.
2. Bind entitlement to a server-side flag on the user record rather than a client-presentable derived token.
3. Rotate both keys after removing them from the repository and `git history`.

```javascript
const ENTITLEMENT_KEY = process.env.ENTITLEMENT_HMAC_KEY
export const deluxeToken = (email: string) =>
  crypto.createHmac('sha256', ENTITLEMENT_KEY).update(email + roles.deluxe).digest('hex')
```

```javascript
case 'tool-call': {

  const isAdmin = decoded?.data?.role === roles.admin

  res.write(/* tool_calls frame */)
  break
```

#### M-065 — Add cosign signing step to release workflow; or use actions/attest-build-provenance

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-065](#f-065) — Container image signing via cosign or attest-build-provenance (`stale.yml:1`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `.github/workflows/stale.yml:1`

```typescript
// Always verify on the public key; never trust the unsigned header.
const decoded = jwt.verify(token, publicKey, { algorithms: ['RS256'] })
```

**Verification:** Tamper one byte in a valid token's payload and confirm `jwt.verify()` throws.

#### M-066 — Use `npm ci --ignore-scripts` and audit required postinstalls separately

- 🟡 [F-066](#f-066) — Dockerfile npm/pnpm/yarn uses --ignore-scripts (`Dockerfile:1`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `test/smoke/Dockerfile:1`

<a id="m-067"></a>
#### M-067 — Hash security answers with a per-user salted adaptive function and a managed secret

**Addresses:**

- 🔴 [F-067](#f-067) — Security answers HMAC'd with hardcoded key (`securityAnswer.ts:45`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Medium · **File:** `lib/insecurity.ts:42`

**How:** Replace the hardcoded-key HMAC in the SecurityAnswer setter with a per-user salted adaptive hash (bcrypt/argon2), the same way passwords should be treated. If a keyed MAC is required, source the key from a secrets manager rather than the `lib/insecurity.ts:42` literal, and rotate it. Normalize answers (trim/lowercase) before hashing to keep comparison correct after the change. Consider deprecating knowledge-based security answers in favor of a stronger recovery factor.

1. Replace the hardcoded-key HMAC in the SecurityAnswer setter with a per-user salted adaptive hash (bcrypt/argon2), the same way passwords should be treated.
2. If a keyed MAC is required, source the key from a secrets manager rather than the `lib/insecurity.ts:42` literal, and rotate it.
3. Normalize answers (trim/lowercase) before hashing to keep comparison correct after the change.
4. Consider deprecating knowledge-based security answers in favor of a stronger recovery factor.

```javascript
answer: {
  type: DataTypes.STRING,
  set (answer: string) {
    this.setDataValue('answer', bcrypt.hashSync(answer.trim().toLowerCase(), 12))
  }
}
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Forgot_Password_Cheat_Sheet.html

---

<a id="m-068"></a>
#### M-068 — Key the reset-password rate limiter on a trusted client identifier

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-068](#f-068) — Rate Limit Bypass via Spoofable Header (`server.ts:346`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Low · **File:** `server.ts:346`

**How:** Configure Express trust proxy correctly and key the limiter on `req.ip` (which express-rate-limit derives from the trusted proxy chain), not the raw X-Forwarded-For header. Add a per-account counter (keyed on the target email) in addition to the per-IP counter so header rotation cannot widen the budget. Lower the max from 100 to a value appropriate for a recovery endpoint (`e.g`. 5 per window).

1. Configure Express trust proxy correctly and key the limiter on `req.ip` (which express-rate-limit derives from the trusted proxy chain), not the raw X-Forwarded-For header.
2. Add a per-account counter (keyed on the target email) in addition to the per-IP counter so header rotation cannot widen the budget.
3. Lower the max from 100 to a value appropriate for a recovery endpoint (`e.g`. 5 per window).

```javascript
app.set('trust proxy', 1)
rateLimit({ windowMs: 5*60*1000, max: 5 }) // default keyGenerator uses req.ip
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Denial_of_Service_Cheat_Sheet.html

---

<a id="m-069"></a>
#### M-069 — Disable DTD/entity expansion and rate-limit XML uploads

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-069](#f-069) — XML Entity Expansion Denial of Service (`fileUpload.ts:76`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Low · **File:** `lib/xml.ts:35`

**How:** Remove `XML_PARSE_DTDLOAD` and `XML_PARSE_NOENT` at `lib/xml.ts:35` so entity-expansion bombs cannot inflate (same change that fixes the XXE finding). Lower the parse timeout and add a per-IP rate limit / concurrency cap on `POST /file-upload` to bound aggregate CPU spend. Require authentication on the route (`server.ts:309`) so the surface is attributable and throttleable per account.

1. Remove `XML_PARSE_DTDLOAD` and `XML_PARSE_NOENT` at `lib/xml.ts:35` so entity-expansion bombs cannot inflate (same change that fixes the XXE finding).
2. Lower the parse timeout and add a per-IP rate limit / concurrency cap on `POST /file-upload` to bound aggregate CPU spend.
3. Require authentication on the route (`server.ts:309`) so the surface is attributable and throttleable per account.

```javascript
// lib/xml.ts:35 — drop NOENT and DTDLOAD
const option = libxml2.ParseOption.XML_PARSE_NOBLANKS | libxml2.ParseOption.XML_PARSE_NOCDATA
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/XML_External_Entity_Prevention_Cheat_Sheet.html

<a id="m-070"></a>
#### M-070 — Add rate limiting and bounded/TTL eviction to web3 wallet tracking sets

**Addresses:**

- 🟡 [F-070](#f-070) — Unbounded in-memory wallet sets, no rate limit (`web3Wallet.ts:16`)

**Priority:** P3 - Next Quarter · **Effort:** Low · **File:** `server.ts:459`

**How:** Apply `rateLimit({ windowMs: 5*60*1000, max: 100 })` (the pattern already used at `server.ts:459`) to the `/rest/web3/walletExploitAddress` and `walletNFTVerify` routes. Replace the unbounded Sets with a bounded LRU/TTL structure so attacker-seeded addresses self-evict; cap maximum entries. Validate `walletAddress` against the EIP-55 address format before storing to reject junk early.

1. Apply `rateLimit({ windowMs: 5*60*1000, max: 100 })` (the pattern already used at `server.ts:459`) to the `/rest/web3/walletExploitAddress` and `walletNFTVerify` routes.
2. Replace the unbounded Sets with a bounded LRU/TTL structure so attacker-seeded addresses self-evict; cap maximum entries.
3. Validate `walletAddress` against the EIP-55 address format before storing to reject junk early.

```javascript
import { rateLimit } from 'express-rate-limit'
const web3Limiter = rateLimit({ windowMs: 5*60*1000, max: 100, validate: false })
app.post('/rest/web3/walletExploitAddress', web3Limiter, utils.asyncHandler(contractExploitListener()))
```

**Reference:** https://cheatsheetseries.owasp.org/cheatsheets/Denial_of_Service_Cheat_Sheet.html

---

### P4 — Backlog

_No P4 mitigations._

---

## 10. Out of Scope

The following items are **explicitly excluded** from this threat model. Findings against these areas should be tracked separately.

- Third-party hosted dependencies and SaaS endpoints
- Browser runtime vulnerabilities and end-user device security
- Operating system kernel and container runtime
- Underlying network infrastructure (DNS, BGP, ISP)
- Physical security of hosting facilities

<a id="appendix-a-vektor-taxonomy"></a>
## Appendix A — Vektor Taxonomy

This appendix defines the attacker-starting-position labels used in the Top Threats table and throughout [§7 Findings Register](#7-findings-register). Each label answers the question *what does the attacker need before the exploit begins?*

<a id="vektor-internet-anon"></a>
### Internet Anon

**Attacker position:** Unauthenticated attacker from the public internet · **Breach distance:** 1

**Preconditions:**

- Endpoint is reachable from the internet (no IP allowlist, no VPN)
- No authentication middleware blocks the request

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-89](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/89.html) · [CWE-79](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/79.html) · [CWE-306](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/306.html) · [CWE-327](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/327.html) · [CWE-611](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/611.html) · [CWE-918](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/918.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A01:2021, A03:2021, A07:2021

<a id="vektor-internet-user"></a>
### Internet User

**Attacker position:** Any authenticated low-privilege user (valid JWT / session) · **Breach distance:** 2

**Preconditions:**

- Attacker has signed up or otherwise obtained a valid user session
- Endpoint is behind auth but not behind role/admin checks

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-434](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/434.html) · [CWE-611](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/611.html) · [CWE-918](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/918.html) · [CWE-352](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/352.html) · [CWE-287](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/287.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A01:2021, A04:2021, A05:2021, A10:2021

<a id="vektor-internet-priv-user"></a>
### Internet Priv User

**Attacker position:** Authenticated admin-level user (JWT with admin role or equivalent) · **Breach distance:** 2

**Preconditions:**

- Attacker holds admin credentials or has elevated privileges
- Endpoint gated on admin role but still exploitable once reached

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-862](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/862.html) · [CWE-79](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/79.html) · [CWE-94](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/94.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A01:2021

<a id="vektor-victim-required"></a>
### Victim-Required

**Attacker position:** Attacker needs victim interaction - social engineering, crafted link, or live session · **Breach distance:** 2

**Preconditions:**

- Victim must click a link, load a page, or have an active session
- Applies to XSS, CSRF, click-jacking, open redirect

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-79](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/79.html) · [CWE-352](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/352.html) · [CWE-601](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/601.html) · [CWE-1021](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1021.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A01:2021, A03:2021

<a id="vektor-build-time"></a>
### Build-Time

**Attacker position:** Attacker controls a build input - CI runner, dependency, base image, or external data fetched during build · **Breach distance:** 3

**Preconditions:**

- Compromise of a dependency, registry, or base image
- OR compromise of a CI runner with write access to artifacts

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-506](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/506.html) · [CWE-829](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/829.html) · [CWE-1039](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1039.html) · [CWE-1104](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/1104.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A08:2021

<a id="vektor-repo-read"></a>
### Repo-Read

**Attacker position:** Attacker gains read access to source repository (leaked clone, forked fork, insider, compromised developer workstation) · **Breach distance:** 3

**Preconditions:**

- Read access to the source tree at or after commit time
- No runtime exploit needed - the vulnerability is the content of the repo

**Typical CWEs:** [CWE-798](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/798.html) · [CWE-312](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/312.html) · [CWE-540](https://cwe.mitre.org/data/definitions/540.html)

**Typical OWASP Top 10:** A02:2021, A07:2021

<a id="vektor-n-a"></a>
### n/a

**Attacker position:** Architectural / meta-finding - no runtime entry point, the finding describes a design defect aggregating multiple code-level findings

**Preconditions:**

- Finding is AF-NNN (architectural) rather than F-NNN (code-level)
